Ruling on Weighing Fees and Order of Payment
States ruling on weighing fees and order of payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state who bears the weighing fee for the price and why, and explain the order of payment when a commodity is sold for currency, applying the Hanafi principle that currency is not determined by specification.

Core Idea
The beneficiary pays for weighing; the buyer pays first to determine the price, then the seller delivers.

This passage from the Book of Sales addresses two practical issues in cash transactions: who pays the weigher's fee for the price, and who must deliver first in case of dispute. The Hanafi school relies on a clear principle—the one who benefits from the service bears the cost—and a fundamental rule about currency not being determined by specification until possession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Locate the two distinct legal rulings presented: (1) allocation of weighing fees for the price versus the commodity, and (2) the order of payment and delivery when a commodity is sold for currency.
The passage begins with the fee ruling, then moves to the order ruling.
2
Understand the principle for fee allocation
The author states that the one for whom the work is done must pay. This is derived from the hadith of cupping, where the Prophet paid the cupper even though the cupping was for him.
The cupping hadith is the proof: 'He got cupping and gave the cupper his fee.'
3
Distinguish between fees for price and commodity
The fee for weighing/testing the price (thaman) is on the buyer because the buyer pays the price and needs to verify it. The fee for measuring/weighing the commodity (e.g., wheat) is on the seller because the seller delivers the commodity.
This distinction follows the same principle: each bears the cost for the service done for them.
4
Grasp the rule that currency is not determined by specification
According to Hanafi fiqh, dirhams, dinars, and modern currency are not determined by specifying a particular coin or note; any unit of equal value suffices until possession. This is derived from the hand-to-hand hadith.
In contrast, commodities like wheat are determined by specification—once specified, a substitute is not allowed.
5
Apply the rule to the order of payment
Because the price is not determined before possession, the buyer must pay first so that the price becomes determined by being taken into the seller's possession. Then the seller delivers the commodity.
This order is obligatory only in case of dispute; by mutual consent, either can act first.

Source Text

حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے پچھنا لگوایا اور آپ نے تجام کو اس کی اجرت دی (ب) آپ نے فرمایا سونا چاندی کے بدلے سود ہے مگر ہاتھوں ہاتھ ہو ۔
The Book of Sales. The fee of weighing the price is on the buyer. [846] Whoever sells a commodity for a price, the buyer is told: pay the price first. When he pays, the seller is told: deliver the sold item. The food: on whom is the fee of measuring? (reference) In an athar, the fee of the measurer is incumbent on the seller. Similarly, if there is need to test the coin, the seller will call an expert to test my coin whether it is genuine or counterfeit. So the fee for testing the coin is on the seller. And since the price is to be paid by the buyer, he will have the coin weighed. Therefore, the weigher's fee must be paid by him, because the weigher did the work for him. The proof is this hadith: from Ibn Abbas: the Prophet (saw) got cupping and gave the cupper his fee. (Bukhari, Bab Kharaj al-Hajjam, no. 2278). Principle: the one for whom the work is done must bear the fee. Explanation: Kiyal: the one who measures. Naqid: the one who tests the coin (dirham, dinar) for genuineness. Wazzan: the one who weighs wheat etc. [846] (27) If someone sold a commodity for a price, the buyer is told to present the price first. When the buyer gives the price, the seller is told to deliver the sold item. The rule is that dirhams and dinars, called primary price, are not determined by specification. For example, if one sold for a five-note and later gave a five-coin, the sale remains valid because their value is equal. Since they are not determined by specification, any can be given. However, after taking possession, dirhams and dinars become determined. The second rule is that commodities, e.g., wheat, grain, are determined by specification. For example, if it is agreed to give five kilos of wheat, one cannot give another five kilos of wheat because that wheat might be bad. When you understand these two rules, understand that when a commodity is sold for dirhams or dinars, the commodity is already determined, while the price (dirhams, dinars, notes) are not determined beforehand. So the buyer is told to present the price first so that the dirhams and dinars become determined by taking possession, and both seller and buyer's rights become equal. Then the seller is told to give the commodity. This ruling is for the time of dispute; otherwise, by mutual consent, either can give first and the sale is valid. The proof that dirhams and dinars are not determined by specification is the indication of this hadith: from Umar: the Messenger of Allah said: Gold for silver is riba except hand-to-hand (ha wa ha), and in another hadith: hand-to-hand (yadan bi-yad). (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Sarf, no. 3349/3348; Tirmidhi). Footnote: (a) The Prophet got cupping and gave the cupper his fee. (b) The Prophet said: Gold for silver is riba except hand-to-hand.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage combines two related rulings. First, it addresses who bears the fee for weighing the price (thaman) in a sale. The author distinguishes between the fee for measuring/weighing the commodity (which is on the seller, as established by athar) and the fee for weighing/testing the price (which is on the buyer, because the buyer is the one who must pay and thus needs to have the price weighed). The principle is clear: the one who commissions the work pays the fee. This is supported by the hadith of cupping, where the Prophet personally paid the cupper, even though the cupping was done for him. Second, the passage explains the order of payment and delivery when a commodity is sold for a price (like dirhams, dinars, or notes). The key legal point is the Hanafi principle that dirhams and dinars (and modern currency) are not 'determined by specification' (تتعين بالتعيين) — meaning that before possession, the buyer can substitute one valid currency for another of equal value. In contrast, commodities (like wheat) are determined by specification: once specified in the contract, the seller must deliver that exact item, not a substitute. Therefore, to ensure both parties' rights are equal, the buyer must pay first so that the price becomes determined by possession; then the seller delivers the commodity. The author notes this rule applies in case of dispute; by mutual consent, the order can vary. The proof that currency is not determined by specification is derived from the hadith emphasizing hand-to-hand exchange (ha wa ha) in currency transactions, which implies that the specific items can be exchanged even after contract as long as possession is simultaneous. The footnote references the same principle.

Key Terms
کیل (kayl): Measurement by volume, often of grains or liquids.
ناقد (naqid): A person who tests coins (dirhams, dinars) to determine if they are genuine or counterfeit.
وزان (wazzān): A person who weighs items such as wheat or other goods.
ثمن (thaman): The price or consideration in a sale, typically dirhams, dinars, or their equivalents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who bears the fee for weighing the price (thaman) in a cash sale?
A) The seller, because he is responsible for the transaction.
B) The buyer, because he is the one who must pay the price.
C) Both equally.
D) The fee is not necessary.

Key Takeaway
The beneficiary pays for weighing services; currency is not determined by specification, so the buyer pays first to determine the price in case of dispute.

Simultaneous Delivery When Goods Are of Same Type
States ruling that both parties must deliver simultaneously when items are of same type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on simultaneous delivery when exchanged items are of the same type and explain the hadith proof.

Core Idea
When both sides of a sale are of the same category, delivery must be simultaneous.

This lesson examines a fundamental rule in the Hanafi law of sales: when the items exchanged are equal in their legal nature (both commodities or both prices), neither party has the right to receive before the other. The obligation to deliver simultaneously is derived from the hadith of Ubadah ibn al-Samit and distinguishes Hanafi fiqh from some other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scenarios
The passage covers two cases: commodity for commodity (sila' bi sila') and price for price (thaman bi thaman). Note that commodities are determined by specification, while prices are not.
2
Understand Why the Ruling Is the Same
When both items are commodities, they are both determined, so their ranks are equal. When both are prices, neither is determined, again equal. In both scenarios, simultaneity is required.
The key concept is equality of legal nature.
3
Examine the Hadith Proof
The hadith from Ubadah ibn al-Samit explicitly commands 'yadan bi yad' (hand-to-hand) for gold-silver and wheat-dates exchanges. This proves that possession must be immediate and simultaneous.
The phrase 'kayfa shi'tum' allows disparity in quantity but not deferment.
4
Note the Practical Consequence
In practice, when parties agree to exchange same-type items, they must complete the exchange in the same session. Neither can claim priority.
This prevents gharar and riba.

اصول سامان متعین ہوتے ہین (۲) شمن یعنی درہم ود نانی متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوتے۔
ال سلعة : سامان شمن : درہم اور دنا نیر کو پیدائشی شمن کہتے ہیں۔ [۸۴۷] (۲۸) اگر سامان کو سامان کے بدلے میں بیچا ، یا من کوشن کے بدلے میں بیچا تو دونوں سے کہا جائے گا کہ ساتھ ساتھ لواور ساتھ ساتھ
طبیع بھی سامان کی قسم ہے اور مشن بھی سامان کی قبیل سے ہے اس لئے دونوں متعین ہیں ۔ اس لئے دونوں کے درجے برابر ہیں ۔اس لئے بائع اور مشتری دونوں سے کہا جائے گا ساتھ ساتھ لو اور ساتھ ساتھ دو۔ ایک کو پہلے اور دوسرے کو بعد میں لینے کا حق نہیں ہے۔ یہی حال ہے جب طبیع بھی درہم یاد تا نیر ہیں اور مشن بھی درہم یاد نا نیر ہیں۔ تو دونوں متعین نہیں ہے اس لئے ایک ساتھ لینے اور ایک ساتھ دینے کے لئے کہا جائیگا۔ حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے عن عبادة بن الصامت عن النبي الله قال . بيعوا الذهب بالفضة كيف شئتم يدا بيد وبيعوا البر بالتمر كيف شئتم يدا بيد (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء ان الحطة بالحنطة مثلا بمثل و کراہیۃ التفاضل فیه ص ۲۳۵ نمبر ۱۲۴۰ ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی الصرف نمبر ۳۳۴۸) اس حدیث میں سونا اور چاندی ایک طرح کے شمن ہیں ، اسی طرح گیہوں اور کھجور ایک طرح کے سامان ہیں تو ایک ہاتھ سے لینے اور دوسرے ہاتھ سے دینے کے لئے کہا۔ اس لئے یدا بید فرمایا گیا۔ چاہے کمی بیشی کے ساتھ نیچے۔

حاشیہ : (الف) نبی نے فرمایا کہ تم سونے کو چاندی کے بدلے میں بیچو جس طرح تم چاہو ہاتھوں ہاتھ اور تم گیہوں کو بچو کھجور کے بدلے میں جس طرح تم چاہو ہاتھوں
ہاتھ۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 2, page 21, Book of Sales. [847] (28) Whoever sells a commodity for a commodity, or a price for a price, both are told: deliver simultaneously. (from the hadith on Sarf, Tirmidhi no. 1243) In this hadith it is said: 'Ha wa ha' – take with one hand and give with the other, i.e., take possession in the session. From this it is understood that dirhams and dinars are not determined by specification. Principle: Commodities are determined by specification. (2) Price (dirhams and dinars) are not determined by specification. Explanation: Sil'a: commodity; thaman: dirhams and dinars are called primary price. [847] (28) If a commodity is sold for a commodity, or a price for a price, both will be told: take together and give together. The commodity is also a type of goods, and the price is also from the category of goods, so both are determined. Therefore, their ranks are equal. So the seller and buyer are both told: take together and give together. Neither has the right to take first and the other later. The same applies when both are dirhams or dinars: both are not determined, so they must take and give simultaneously. Proof is the hadith from Ubadah ibn al-Samit from the Prophet (saw): 'Sell gold for silver as you wish, hand-to-hand; and sell wheat for dates as you wish, hand-to-hand.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a anna al-hinta bi al-hintha mithlan bi mithl, no. 1240; Abu Dawud, Bab al-Sarf, no. 3348) In this hadith, gold and silver are one type of price; similarly, wheat and dates are one type of commodity. So they are told to take with one hand and give with the other, thus 'yadan bi yad' (hand-to-hand), even if there is excess or deficiency. Footnote: (a) The Prophet said: Sell gold for silver as you wish, hand-to-hand, and sell wheat for dates as you wish, hand-to-hand.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when the exchanged items are of the same legal category. The author presents two cases: (1) commodity for commodity (sila' bi sila') and (2) price for price (thaman bi thaman). When both items are commodities, they are both determined by specification (mu'ayyan), so neither party has an advantage; both must deliver simultaneously. When both items are prices (like dirhams and dinars), neither is determined by specification, so again simultaneous delivery is required. The underlying principle is that when the two items are equal in their legal nature (both mithli or both thaman), the obligation to perform is equal, and no one can claim priority. The proof is the hadith of Ubadah ibn al-Samit, which explicitly permits gold-for-silver (both prices) and wheat-for-dates (both commodities) only if it is hand-to-hand (yadan bi yad). The Hadith allows disparity in quantity (e.g., more gold for less silver) as long as possession is simultaneous. The footnote confirms the hadith. The author also notes that this hadith also proves that dirhams and dinars are not determined by specification (since hand-to-hand is required).

Key Terms
سلعة (sila'): Commodity or good that is sold, as opposed to price (thaman).
ثمن (thaman): Price or consideration, especially dirhams, dinars, or their equivalents, which are not determined by specification before possession.
يدا بيد (yadan bi yad): Hand-to-hand, meaning immediate and simultaneous exchange of both items in the contract session.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a commodity is sold for another commodity, what is the ruling regarding delivery according to this passage?
A) The buyer must deliver first.
B) The seller must deliver first.
C) Both must deliver simultaneously.
D) They may agree on any order.

Key Takeaway
When the exchanged items are equal in legal category, simultaneous delivery is wajib, grounded in the hadith hand-to-hand command.

Khiyar al-Shart: Permissibility and Duration in Hanafi Fiqh
states and proves the permissibility of stipulating an option in a sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-shart, explain its permissibility, and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the maximum duration.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-shart is permissible for three days only, according to Abu Hanifa, based on the hadith 'or the sale is conditional'.

In this passage, the author establishes that stipulating an option in a sale is valid. He explains the mechanism, the maximum period, and provides the prophetic proof. However, there is an internal Hanafi disagreement on the duration — you will learn which view is relied upon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states that khiyar al-shart is permissible (ja'iz) in a sale for both the seller and the buyer. Note that it is a right, not an obligation.
2
Understand the mechanism of khiyar al-shart
After offer and acceptance, either party may stipulate an option for a specified period. During that period, the stipulator may confirm or cancel the sale. If the period expires without cancellation, the sale becomes binding.
The option must be agreed upon at the time of the contract.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi disagreement on duration
Abu Hanifa restricts the option to a maximum of three days. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani allow a longer period if specified, as long as it is known.
The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is three days, though later fatwa sometimes follows the Sahibayn.
4
Analyze the dalil
The hadith of Ibn 'Umar states: 'The two parties have an option as long as they have not separated or the sale is conditional (khiyar).' The phrase 'او يكون البيع خيارا' is the proof — it indicates that a sale can be made conditional by stipulating an option.
The dalal: the phrase directly permits khiyar al-shart.

باب خيار الشرط [۸۴۸(۱) خيار الشرط جائز فى البيع للبائع والمشترى [۴۹] (۲) ولهما الخيار ثلثة ايام فما دونها ولا يجوز اكثر من ذلك عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى وقال ابو يوسف و و باب خیار الشرط ضروری نوٹ خیار شرط کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ایجاب و قبول ہونے کے بعد مجلس میں رہتے ہوئے بائع یا مشتری دونوں یہ کہے کہ ہمیں تین دن کا اختیار دیں اس تین دن میں چاہوں تو طبیع لو اور چاہوں تو بیع رد کر دوں۔ اور سامنے والا اسپر ہاں کہہ دے تو اس کو خیار شرط کہتے ہیں۔ اب اس کو اختیار ہوگا کہ چاہے تو بائع جائز قرار دے اور چاہے تو بیع تو ڑ دے۔ البتہ اگر تین دن تک بیع کو نہیں تو ڑا تو بیع برقرار ہے گی۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عـمـر عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ان المتبايعين بالخيار في بيعهما مالم يتفرقا او يكون البيع خيارا (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب کم یجوز الخیار ص ۲۸۳ نمبر ۲۱۰۷ ر مسلم شریف ، باب ثبوت خیار مجلس للمتبايعين ج ثانی ص ۶ نمبر ۱۵۳۱ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب فی خیار المتبایعین ج ثانی ص ۱۳۳ نمبر ۳۴۵۴) اس حدیث کے لفظ او يكون البیع خیارا سے معلوم ہوا کہ بائع اور مشتری کو خیار شرط ملے گا۔ [۸۴۸] (۱) خیار شرط جائز ہے بیچ میں بائع کے لئے اور مشتری کے لئے۔ ایجاب اور قبول ہونے کے بعد اگر دونوں یا ایک خیار شرط لے لے تو اس کو خیار شرط ملے گا۔ او پر حدیث گزرگئی ہے کہ متبایعین یعنی بائع اور مشتری دونوں کو خیار شرط لینے پر خیار شرط ملے گا۔
Chapter on the Option of Stipulation. [848] (1) The option of stipulation is permissible in a sale for the seller and the buyer. [849] (2) And both have the option for three days or less, and it is not permissible to exceed that according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said... Necessary note: The meaning of khiyar al-shart is that after offer and acceptance, while still in the session, the seller or buyer says: 'Give us an option for three days; within these three days, if I wish I will take the goods, and if I wish I will reject the sale.' And the other says 'yes'. This is called khiyar al-shart. Then he will have the option: if he wishes, he confirms the sale, and if he wishes, he cancels it. However, if he does not cancel the sale within three days, the sale becomes binding. Its proof is the hadith of Ibn 'Umar from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The two parties in a transaction have an option as long as they have not separated or the sale is conditional (khiyar).' From the phrase 'or the sale is conditional', it is understood that the seller and buyer have the option of stipulation. [848] (1) Khiyar al-shart is permissible in a sale for the seller and the buyer. After offer and acceptance, if both or one takes the option, he will have the option of stipulation. The hadith above has passed that the two transacting parties, i.e., seller and buyer, when they stipulate an option, will have the option of stipulation.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on Khiyar al-Shart (option of stipulation). It first states that khiyar al-shart is permissible in a sale for both the seller and the buyer. The author explains the mechanism: after the offer and acceptance (ijab and qabul), either party or both may stipulate an option for a specified period (usually up to three days). During this period, the stipulator may either complete the sale or rescind it. If the option period expires without rescission, the sale becomes binding. The proof is the hadith of Ibn 'Umar in which the Prophet said that the two parties have an option as long as they have not separated or unless the sale is made conditional (khiyar). The phrase 'or the sale is conditional' (أو يكون البيع خيارا) is taken as evidence for khiyar al-shart. Thus, the school establishes the permissibility of this type of option.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in the contract that allows one or both parties to cancel the sale within a specified period.
متبايعان (mutabayi'ani): The two transacting parties: the seller and the buyer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the evidence for the permissibility of khiyar al-shart according to this passage?
A) The hadith 'The two parties have an option as long as they have not separated or the sale is conditional.'
B) Consensus of the companions.
C) Qiyas on khiyar al-majlis.
D) The Quranic verse on fulfilling contracts.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-shart is a valid right for both parties, limited to three days according to Abu Hanifa, with the Sahibayn allowing longer periods.

Duration of Khiyar al-Shart: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
presents intra-Hanafi dispute on maximum duration of stipulated option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the maximum duration of khiyar al-shart and explain the basis for the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The option of stipulation is limited to three days according to Abu Hanifa; exceeding it harms the other party.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: how long can the buyer and seller stipulate an option (khiyar al-shart) before the sale becomes binding? Imam Abu Hanifa sets a strict three-day limit based on a specific hadith and the principle of avoiding harm, while his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, argue that the parties may agree on any specified period. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school balances textual evidence and party autonomy.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on khiyar al-shart duration
Identify which view is attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa and which to the Sahibayn. Abu Hanifa holds that the option period cannot exceed three days; the Sahibayn allow any agreed period as long as it is known.
The option period must be specified in both views.
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's proofs
Analyze the two proofs Abu Hanifa presents: (1) the hadith 'al-khiyar thalathatu ayyam' and (2) the principle of avoiding harm (dharar) to the other party who must wait.
The hadith is considered a specific textual proof (dalil khas) that restricts the general permissibility of stipulations.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's proofs
The Sahibayn rely on the general permissibility of stipulations (al-mu'minun 'ala shurutihim) and argue that as long as both parties consent, any known period is valid. They do not interpret the three-day hadith as a binding limit.
They may view the hadith as non-mutawatir or as a preference, not a requirement.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If a buyer and seller agree to a five-day option, what is the ruling? Per Abu Hanifa, the option period is invalid and the sale becomes binding immediately at the time of contract. Per the Sahibayn, the five-day option is valid and the sale is suspended until the period ends.
This difference affects whether the buyer can still rescind the sale after three days.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (relied-upon position)
The Hanafi school has adopted Abu Hanifa's view as the mufta bihi, as it is based on a stronger textual proof and greater caution (ihtiyat). However, in some later practice, especially in custom-heavy contracts, longer periods may be allowed by some scholars.
The text favors Abu Hanifa by presenting his proofs in detail.

(ب) امام ابو حنيفة کی دلیل: (۱) تین دن سے زیادہ کا اختیار لینے میں سامنے والے آدمی کو نقصان ہو گا کہ بہت دنوں تک اس کو انتظار کر نا ہوگا کہ بیچ ہوئی یا نہیں ۔اس لئے تین دن سے زیادہ اختیار نہیں دیا جائے (۲) حدیث میں تین دن کے ہی اختیار کا ثبوت ہے عن ابن عمر عن النبي الله قال الخيار ثلاثة ايام (ب) ( دارقطني ، كتاب البيوع ج ثالث ص ۲۸ نمبر ۲۹۹۳ رسنن بیھقی ، باب الدلیل علی ان لا یجوز شرط الخيار في الصبیح اکثر من ثلاثۃ ایام ج خامس ص ۴۵۰ نمبر ۱۰۴۶۱ارترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی المصر اق ص ۲۳۶ نمبر ۱۲۵۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ صرف تین دن کا اختیار ملے گا۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ خیار شرط کا معاملہ بائع اور مشتری کے اختیار پر ہے اس لئے اگر وہ دونوں زیادہ دنوں تک اختیار دینے پر راضی ہیں تو کسی حاشیہ : آپ نے فرمایا بائع اور مشتری کو اختیار ہے بیچ میں جب تک کہ دونوں جدا نہ ہو جائیں یا بیچ میں خیار شرط ہو ( ب ) آپ نے فرمایا خیار شرط تین دن تک ہوتا
[849] (2) And both have the option for three days or less, and it is not permissible to exceed that according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is permissible if the period is specified. Abu Hanifa's proof: (1) Taking an option for more than three days harms the other party as he has to wait many days to know whether the sale is concluded. (2) The hadith proves only three days: from Ibn 'Umar from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The option is for three days.' (Darqutni, Bayhaqi, Tirmidhi). The Sahibayn say that the matter of khiyar al-shart is at the discretion of the seller and buyer, so if they both agree to give a longer period, then... Marginal note: The Prophet said: 'The two parties have an option in the sale as long as they have not separated or the sale is conditional.' (b) The Prophet said: 'The option of stipulation is for three days.'
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the maximum duration of khiyar al-shart. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the option cannot exceed three days. He provides two proofs: first, a longer period would cause harm (dharar) to the other party who must wait to know the fate of the contract; second, there is a specific hadith from Ibn 'Umar stating 'the option is for three days' (الخيار ثلاثة أيام). On the other hand, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue that the option is a matter of mutual agreement; if both parties consent, a longer period is permissible. They rely on the general permissibility of stipulations agreed upon by both parties. The text also repeats the hadith mentioned earlier about the option until separation or conditional sale. The dispute illustrates the Hanafi methodology of balancing textual evidence (the three-day hadith) and the principle of party autonomy. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa, limiting the option to three days, though some later scholars have permitted longer periods in cases of necessity.

Key Terms
مدة (mudda): Duration of the stipulated option period.
صاحبان (sahibayn): The two companions: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, principal students of Abu Hanifa.
خيار شرط (khiyar al-shart): A stipulated option in a sale contract, allowing one or both parties to cancel the sale within a specified period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) As agreed by the parties
C) Three days
D) One year

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, khiyar al-shart is limited to three days based on a specific hadith and the principle of preventing harm, although the Sahibayn allowed longer periods by mutual agreement.

Khiyar al-Shart: Permissibility and Proof
Ruling on khiyar al-shart with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of khiyar al-shart, identify its proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar, and explain the key conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-shart is permissible; the hadith's phrase 'au yakuna al-bai'u khiyaran' directly proves it.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation) in sales. The source passage states that this option is permissible for both seller and buyer after offer and acceptance, provided a three-day period is agreed upon. The primary evidence is a well-known hadith narrated by Ibn Umar. Understanding this ruling helps you distinguish permitted conditions from those that invalidate a contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what legal act is being described (khiyar al-shart) and its hukm level (mubah/permissible) according to the text.
The text explicitly says 'ja'iz' (permissible) for both parties.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the scriptural proof cited – here it is the hadith of Ibn Umar narrated by Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud.
The hadith is: 'The two parties in a sale have an option as long as they have not separated, or the sale is with an option.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze the specific phrase in the hadith that yields the ruling – 'au yakuna al-bai'u khiyaran' (or the sale is with an option). This indicates that stipulating an option in the sale contract is valid.
The phrase shows the sale itself can be made conditional on an option, which is the basis of khiyar al-shart.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Check if there is disagreement among the Hanafi imams or other schools. The text indicates no intra-Hanafi difference; all agree on permissibility. However, the Shafi'i school allows a longer period if agreed upon.
The Hanafi limit is three days; this is a point of cross-madhhab difference.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling) from the text. Since it is agreed upon, the ruling is clear: khiyar al-shart is permissible for both parties.
The commentary states the ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and there is no conflict.

باب خيار الشرط
[۸۴۸(۱) خيار الشرط جائز فى البيع للبائع والمشترى
ضروری نوٹ خیار شرط کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ایجاب و قبول ہونے کے بعد مجلس میں رہتے ہوئے بائع یا مشتری دونوں یہ کہے کہ ہمیں تین دن کا اختیار دیں اس تین دن میں چاہوں تو طبیع لو اور چاہوں تو بیع رد کر دوں۔ اور سامنے والا اسپر ہاں کہہ دے تو اس کو خیار شرط کہتے ہیں۔ اب اس کو اختیار ہوگا کہ چاہے تو بائع جائز قرار دے اور چاہے تو بیع تو ڑ دے۔ البتہ اگر تین دن تک بیع کو نہیں تو ڑا تو بیع برقرار ہے گی۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عـمـر عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ان المتبايعين بالخيار في بيعهما مالم يتفرقا او يكون البيع خيارا (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب کم یجوز الخیار ص ۲۸۳ نمبر ۲۱۰۷ ر مسلم شریف ، باب ثبوت خیار مجلس للمتبايعين ج ثانی ص ۶ نمبر ۱۵۳۱ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب فی خیار المتبایعین ج ثانی ص ۱۳۳ نمبر ۳۴۵۴) اس حدیث کے لفظ او يكون البیع خیارا سے معلوم ہوا کہ بائع اور مشتری کو خیار شرط ملے گا۔
[۸۴۸] (۱) خیار شرط جائز ہے بیچ میں بائع کے لئے اور مشتری کے لئے۔
ایجاب اور قبول ہونے کے بعد اگر دونوں یا ایک خیار شرط لے لے تو اس کو خیار شرط ملے گا۔
او پر حدیث گزرگئی ہے کہ متبایعین یعنی بائع اور مشتری دونوں کو خیار شرط لینے پر خیار شرط ملے گا۔
Chapter of the Option of Stipulation. [848] (1) The option of stipulation is permissible in the sale for the seller and the buyer. Essential Note: The meaning of khiyar al-shart is that after offer and acceptance while still in the session, the seller or buyer says: 'Give us an option of three days; within these three days, if I wish I will take the item and if I wish I will revoke the sale.' And the other party agrees, so this is called khiyar al-shart. Then he will have the option: if he wishes, he can make the sale binding, and if he wishes, he can break the sale. However, if he does not break the sale within three days, the sale becomes binding. Its proof is this hadith from Ibn 'Umar from the Prophet (peace be upon him): he said: 'The two parties in a sale have an option as long as they have not separated, or the sale is with an option.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud). From the words of this hadith 'or the sale is with an option', it is understood that the seller and buyer have the option of stipulation. [848] (1) The option of stipulation is permissible in the sale for the seller and the buyer. After offer and acceptance, if both or one takes the option of stipulation, then he will have the option of stipulation. The hadith has passed that the two parties to a sale, i.e., the seller and buyer, both have the option of stipulation if they take the option of stipulation.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Khiyar al-Shart (option of stipulation). The author states the first ruling: this option is permissible for both seller and buyer. The commentator then explains the mechanism: after offer and acceptance (which constitute the contract), while still in the session, one party may request a three-day period to decide. If the other agrees, the condition is valid. The proof is the famous hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet said the two parties have an option as long as they have not separated or the sale is with an option. The phrase 'or the sale is with an option' directly supports khiyar al-shart. The commentary clarifies that the option is effective once stipulated; if the option period expires without cancellation, the sale becomes binding. This ruling is part of the Zahir al-Riwayah and is agreed upon by all Hanafi imams.

Key Terms
خیار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): A condition in a sale contract granting one or both parties the right to cancel within a specified period, usually three days.
ایجاب و قبول (ijab wa qabul): Offer and acceptance, the essential components of a contract in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary textual proof for the permissibility of khiyar al-shart according to this passage?
A) The hadith 'The seller and buyer have an option as long as they have not separated or the sale is with an option'
B) The hadith 'The buyer has an option for three days'
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Analogy to khiyar al-majlis

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-shart is a permissible condition in a sale, limited to three days, and is proven by the Prophet's hadith where he allowed a sale to be with an option.

Duration of Khiyar al-Shart: The Three-Day Limit
Dispute on maximum duration of khiyar al-shart

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the maximum duration of khiyar al-shart and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-shart is limited to three days per the mufta bihi view, based on explicit hadith and preventing harm.

This passage presents an internal Hanafi disagreement on how long a khiyar al-shart can last. Abu Hanifa restricts it to three days, while his two main students allow any agreed known period. Understanding this ikhtilaf helps you see how the school weighs textual evidence against party autonomy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
Identify the act as khiyar al-shart (an option period to confirm or rescind a sale) and the disputed condition as its maximum duration.
Khiyar al-shart is a condition in a sale contract allowing one or both parties to rescind within a specified time.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Abu Hanifa holds that the option cannot exceed three days. His evidence is the hadith 'al-khiyar thalathatu ayyam' and the principle of preventing harm (darar) to the other party.
The hadith is narrated by Ibn 'Umar and recorded by Darqutni, Bayhaqi, and Tirmidhi.
3
State Sahibayn's position and their dalil
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the option can be for any known period as long as it is specified, based on general permission and mutual consent.
They interpret the hadith as not imposing a strict limit.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The school responds that the specific hadith restricts the general; allowing longer periods leads to uncertainty (gharar) and harm. Thus Abu Hanifa's view is preferred.
The principle of preventing darar overrides party autonomy in this case.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah al-khilaf
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's: the option is limited to three days. Practically, a four-day option is invalid per Abu Hanifa but valid per Sahibayn.
The condition is void if it exceeds three days, and the sale becomes binding immediately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۸۴۹ (۲) بائع اور مشتری دونوں کو تین دن یا اس سے کم کا اختیار ہوگا۔ اور نہیں جائز ہے اس سے زیادہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اور کہا امام ابو ابو یوسف اور امام محمد نے کہ جائز ہے جبکہ مدت معلوم متعین کر دے۔
تین دن سے زیادہ کا اختیار لے تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک تین دن سے زیادہ کا اختیار نہیں ملے گا۔
(۱) تین دن سے زیادہ کا اختیار لینے میں سامنے والے آدمی کو نقصان ہو گا کہ بہت دنوں تک اس کو انتظار کر نا ہوگا کہ بیچ ہوئی یا نہیں ۔اس لئے تین دن سے زیادہ اختیار نہیں دیا جائے (۲) حدیث میں تین دن کے ہی اختیار کا ثبوت ہے عن ابن عمر عن النبي الله قال الخيار ثلاثة ايام (ب) ( دارقطني ، كتاب البيوع ج ثالث ص ۲۸ نمبر ۲۹۹۳ رسنن بیھقی ، باب الدلیل علی ان لا یجوز شرط الخيار في الصبیح اکثر من ثلاثۃ ایام ج خامس ص ۴۵۰ نمبر ۱۰۴۶۱ارترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی المصر اق ص ۲۳۶ نمبر ۱۲۵۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ صرف تین دن کا اختیار ملے گا۔
صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ خیار شرط کا معاملہ بائع اور مشتری کے اختیار پر ہے اس لئے اگر وہ دونوں زیادہ دنوں تک اختیار دینے پر راضی ہیں تو کسی حاشیہ : آپ نے فرمایا بائع اور مشتری کو اختیار ہے بیچ میں جب تک کہ دونوں جدا نہ ہو جائیں یا بیچ میں خیار شرط ہو ( ب ) آپ نے فرمایا خیار شرط تین دن تک ہوتا
[849] (2) The seller and buyer both have an option of three days or less. And it is not permissible more than that according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad said that it is permissible as long as he specifies a known period. If he takes an option of more than three days, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, an option of more than three days will not be granted. (1) Taking an option of more than three days would cause harm to the other party because he would have to wait many days to know if the sale happened or not. Therefore, an option of more than three days is not given. (2) In the hadith, there is proof for an option of only three days: from Ibn 'Umar from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: 'The option is for three days.' (Darqutni, Bayhaqi, Tirmidhi). From this hadith, it is understood that only a three-day option will be granted. The Sahibayn say that the matter of khiyar al-shart is up to the seller and buyer; therefore if both are agreeable to giving an option for more days, there is no problem. Their evidence is the above hadith which does not limit to three days absolutely; the option is given unconditionally.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the maximum duration of khiyar al-shart. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the option period cannot exceed three days, based on two reasons: (1) longer periods cause hardship to the other party who must wait in uncertainty, and (2) the hadith 'al-khiyar thalathatu ayyam' (the option is for three days) explicitly sets the limit. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue that since khiyar al-shart is based on mutual agreement, it should be permissible for any known period, as long as it is specified. They rely on the general hadith about the option without the three-day restriction. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa: the option is limited to three days. This is the stronger view due to the explicit hadith and the principle that excessive uncertainty (gharar) is avoided. The term 'known period' (mudda ma'luma) is key: the Sahibayn require that the period be definite, not unknown.

Key Terms
مدة معلومة (mudda ma'luma): A known, definite period; if the period is unspecified (majhul), the condition is invalid.
صاحبین (al-Sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two main students of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on the maximum duration of khiyar al-shart?
A) Any known period as agreed by the parties.
B) Three days.
C) Two days.
D) No limit; it varies.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-shart is limited to three days per Abu Hanifa's view, which is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, based on explicit hadith and the principle of preventing harm.

Seller's Option and Ownership Transfer
Ruling: seller's option prevents ownership transfer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the effect of khiyar al-shart on ownership and apply the ruling to determine who can exercise ownership acts during the option period.

Core Idea
With khiyar al-shart, ownership of the sold item stays with the seller until full consent is given.

In a sale with an option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart), the seller reserves the right to cancel within a specified period. This lesson clarifies that during that period, the sold item remains in the seller's ownership even if physically possessed by the buyer. We will examine the ruling, its practical implications, and the hadith evidence from Abu Huraira that supports it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The passage addresses what happens to ownership of the sold item (mabi') when the seller has a khiyar al-shart. Determine whether ownership transfers immediately or remains suspended.
The key is that the sale is valid but non-binding (ghayr lazim).
2
State the ruling
The seller's option prevents the mabi' from leaving his ownership during the option period. Even if the buyer takes physical possession, the seller remains the owner.
This is a clear ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Derive practical consequences
Since ownership remains with the seller, he alone can perform acts of ownership (e.g., freeing a slave). The buyer cannot do so, as he does not yet own the item.
This distinction is crucial for understanding legal capacity during khiyar.
4
Analyze the proof
The hadith 'La yaftariqan 'an bai'in illa 'an taradin' is cited. It conditions separation on mutual consent. The seller's consent is not fully given until the option is resolved, so the sale is not final and ownership does not transfer.
The hadith is ahad (zanni thubut) but is sufficient for this ruling in Hanafi usul.
5
Note the authority level
This position is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi. While later Hanafis discuss nuances of risk, the core rule remains unchanged.
Cross-madhhab status: mukhtalaf fih with some schools; but within Hanafi, it is agreed upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۸۵۰] (۳) بائع کا اختیار روکتا ہے مبیع کے نکلنے کو اس کی ملکیت سے۔
بائع نے خیار شرطا لیا تو چاہے مبیع مشتری کے ہاتھ میں جاچکی ہو لیکن ابھی بھی وہ بائع کی ملکیت ہی میں ہے۔ اس کی ملکیت سے نکلی نہیں
بائع نے اختیار کیا تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بیع کرنے کے باوجود وہ ابھی اپنی ملکیت میں رکھنا چاہتا ہے۔ جب وہ بیچ نافذ کرے گا تب اس کی ملکیت سے مبیع نکلے گی۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ وہ اس دوران مبیع کو آزاد کرنا چاہے تو آزاد کر سکتا ہے، اور مشتری آزاد کرنا چاہے تو نہیں کر سکتا کیونکہ اس کی ملکیت میں ابھی مبیع نہیں گئی ہے۔ اسوال بائع کی پوری رضامندی کے بغیر مبیع اس کے ہاتھ سے نہیں نکلے گی۔ حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے عن ابي هريرة عن النبي الله قال لا يفترقن عن بيع الا عن تراض (الف) (ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی خیار المتبایعین ص ۲۳۶ نمبر ۱۲۴۸ را بود او دشریف، باب خیار المتبایعین ص ۱۳۳ نمبر ۳۳۵۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ رضامندی کے بغیر بائع اور مشتری جدا نہ ہوں۔ اس لئے خیار شرط کی وجہ سے بائع کی ملکیت سے بیع نہیں نکلے گی۔
[850] (3) The seller's option prevents the sale item from exiting his ownership. If the seller takes the option of stipulation, even if the sale item has reached the buyer's hand, it is still in the seller's ownership. It has not left his ownership. When the seller takes the option, it means that despite the sale, he still wants to keep the item in his ownership. When he enforces the sale, then the sale item will leave his ownership. This is why during this period, if he wants to emancipate the item (e.g., free a slave), he can do so, and the buyer cannot emancipate it because it has not yet entered his ownership. As a point: the sale item will not leave the seller's hand without his full consent. There is an indication of this in the hadith from Abu Huraira from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The two parties should not separate from a sale except with mutual consent' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud). In this hadith, it is that the seller and buyer should not separate without consent. Therefore, due to the option of stipulation, the sale item does not leave the seller's ownership.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage explains the legal consequence of the seller having an option of stipulation: the sold item remains in the seller's ownership during the option period. Even if the buyer takes physical possession, ownership does not transfer until the seller confirms the sale. The commentator draws two practical implications: (1) the seller can still perform acts of ownership, such as emancipating a slave (which would nullify the sale because it implies ownership), while the buyer cannot; (2) the sale becomes binding only with the seller's full consent. The proof is the hadith prohibiting separation without mutual consent, which implies that without final consent (which the seller has yet to give due to the option), ownership does not transfer. This ruling is consistent with the principle that khiyar prevents the sale from becoming binding (lazim) and thus ownership does not pass. It is a standard Hanafi ruling from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
مبیع (mabi'): The item being sold; the subject matter of the sale.
رضامندی (raza mandi): Consent (rida); here it refers to the seller's final approval to execute the sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
During the seller's option period, can the buyer free a slave that was sold with khiyar al-shart?
A) Yes, because the buyer has possession
B) No, because ownership remains with the seller
C) Yes, with the seller's permission
D) No, unless the option period has expired

Key Takeaway
Ownership during khiyar al-shart remains with the seller; acts of ownership by the buyer are invalid.

Buyer's Liability for Item Perishing During Option
Ruling on buyer's liability when item perishes during seller's option period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the buyer's liability when an item perishes during the seller's option period and apply the ruling to similar scenarios using the proof from Qadi Shurayh's judgment.

Core Idea
If a sale is not finalised, the buyer is still liable for market value if the item perishes in his possession during the option period.

You know that a sale with an option (khiyar) is not immediately binding. But what happens if the buyer takes the item home and it is destroyed? Does he owe anything? This lesson clarifies that the buyer is not free from liability even though the sale might not go through. We will see why the Hanafi school holds the buyer liable for the market value, not the agreed price, and the strong evidence from the practice of the Companion 'Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The text describes a case where the seller stipulates a three-day option, the buyer takes possession, and the item is destroyed. Note that the sale is not yet concluded.
Option (khiyar) can be for either party; here it is the seller's option.
2
Determine the buyer's liability
The buyer must pay the market value (qimat), not the agreed price. Why? Because the item was taken as a trial (saum), not as a final purchase.
Liability is wajib, not optional.
3
Examine the proof: the athar of 'Umar and Shurayh
Qadi Shurayh ruled that 'Umar was a guarantor (dammin) for the horse until returned sound. This establishes liability for any loss during the option period.
The athar is from Bayhaqi and Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Understand the rationale
Ownership did not transfer to the buyer (the seller still owns it), but the buyer's possession creates a guarantee. The buyer is not a mere trustee (amin) but bears risk.
Hanafi: strict liability during option period.
5
Apply the ruling to analogous cases
For example, if you test-drive a car with an option to buy and crash it, you owe the market value, not the agreed price.
This applies to any item taken on trial with seller's permission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[851] (4) Then if the buyer takes possession of the sale item and it perishes in his hand during the option period, he is liable for its value. If the seller had taken a three-day option of stipulation and the buyer took possession of the item with the seller's permission, and thereafter the item perished in the buyer's hand, then the price agreed between seller and buyer does not become binding. But he must pay the market value of that item that day. Because the seller had the option, so the item did not leave his ownership and the sale was not concluded. But the buyer had taken it by way of bargaining, and it perished, so the market value is incumbent upon him. The proof of this is in the athar (report from a Companion). 'Umar bought a horse from a man, saying if I like it I will keep it. Then he had a man ride it, causing a defect. 'Umar accepted the judgment of Qadi Shurayh, who said: 'You took it sound and whole, and you are its guarantor until you return it sound and whole.' (Bayhaqi, Abd al-Razzaq). From this athar it is understood...
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where the buyer takes possession of the sold item during the seller's option period and the item perishes or is damaged in the buyer's hands. The ruling is that the sale is not binding (since the seller has the option to cancel), but the buyer is liable for the market value (qimat) of the item, not the agreed price. This is because the buyer took possession on the basis of a potential sale (bi tareeq al-saum, i.e., bargaining or trial), similar to khiyar al-shart. The buyer is considered a guarantor (amin) but with liability for loss. The proof is the well-known incident of 'Umar and Qadi Shurayh: 'Umar bought a horse with a condition of inspection, and after using it, it became defective. Shurayh ruled that 'Umar must either return it in the same condition or pay its value. This establishes the principle that anyone who takes possession of an item under a condition of option is liable for its value if it perishes, because the ownership has not transferred. The commentary notes that the agreed price is not binding; instead, the market value is owed.

Key Terms
ضامن (dammin): Liable; here the buyer must compensate the seller by paying the market value of the item.
قیمت (qimat): Market value of the item at the time of loss, not the agreed price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Nothing
C) The market value
D) Half the market value

Key Takeaway
A buyer who takes possession of an item during an option period is a guarantor and must pay the market value if the item is lost or destroyed.

Seller's Khiyar al-Shart Prevents Transfer of Ownership
States ruling with proof that seller's option prevents ownership transfer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the effect of khiyar al-shart on ownership transfer and identify the proof from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
Seller's option keeps ownership; buyer's possession is at risk until consent is finalized.

In this lesson we examine a key rule in sales: when the seller stipulates an option (khiyar al-shart), the sold item does not leave the seller's ownership during the option period. Even if the buyer takes possession, he does not become owner. If the item perishes, liability is based on market value, not the agreed price. The proof comes from a hadith that stresses mutual consent for sale completion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the ruling: the seller's option prevents the sold item from leaving his ownership during the option period. Note that the period must be known and specified.
This is the core legal effect.
2
Analyze the hadith proof
Examine the hadith: 'Do not separate from a sale except with mutual consent.' Explain how the phrase 'illa 'an taradin' requires full consent for the sale to be final. Since the seller has not given full consent due to his option, the sale remains incomplete.
The hadith is from Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud.
3
Analyze the athar proof
Review the case of 'Umar and Shurayh: 'Umar took a horse on trial, caused a defect, and Shurayh ruled he was liable for the market value. This establishes that in option-based possession, liability is for market value, not the agreed price.
This athar is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Understand the practical implication
If the buyer takes possession during the option period and the item perishes, the buyer must pay the market value (qima) at the time of loss. The buyer cannot dispose of the item (e.g., free a slave) because ownership has not transferred.
This distinguishes khiyar al-shart from a final sale.

Source Text

كتاب البيوع
محمد يجوز اذا سمى مدة معلومة ( ۸۵۰ (۳) و خيار البائع يمنع خروج المبيع من ملكه
[۸۵۱](۴) فان قبضه المشترى فهلک بیده فى مدة الخيار ضمنه بالقيمة کو کوئی اشکال نہیں ہونا چاہئے بشرطیکہ مدت معلوم ہو کہ کتنے دنوں کا اختیار لینا چاہتے ہیں، مجہول نہ ہو۔ ان کی دلیل اوپر کی حدیث ہے جس میں تین دن کی قید نہیں ہے مطلقا اختیار دیا گیا ہے۔
[۸۵۰] (۳) بائع کا اختیار روکتا ہے مبیع کے نکلنے کو اس کی ملکیت سے۔
بائع نے خیار شرطا لیا تو چاہے مبیع مشتری کے ہاتھ میں جاچکی ہو لیکن ابھی بھی وہ بائع کی ملکیت ہی میں ہے۔ اس کی ملکیت سے نکلی نہیں
بائع نے اختیار کیا تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بیع کرنے کے باوجود وہ ابھی اپنی ملکیت میں رکھنا چاہتا ہے۔ جب وہ بیچ نافذ کرے گا تب اس کی ملکیت سے مبیع نکلے گی۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ وہ اس دوران مبیع کو آزاد کرنا چاہے تو آزاد کر سکتا ہے، اور مشتری آزاد کرنا چاہے تو نہیں کر سکتا کیونکہ اس کی ملکیت میں ابھی مبیع نہیں گئی ہے۔ اسوال بائع کی پوری رضامندی کے بغیر مبیع اس کے ہاتھ سے نہیں نکلے گی۔ حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے عن ابي هريرة عن النبي الله قال لا يفترقن عن بيع الا عن تراض (الف) (ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی خیار المتبایعین ص ۲۳۶ نمبر ۱۲۴۸ را بود او دشریف، باب خیار المتبایعین ص ۱۳۳ نمبر ۳۳۵۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ رضامندی کے بغیر بائع اور مشتری جدا نہ ہوں۔ اس لئے خیار شرط کی وجہ سے بائع کی ملکیت سے بیع نہیں نکلے گی۔
[۸۵۱) (۴۳) پس اگر مشتری نے مبیع پر قبضہ کیا اور مدت خیار میں اس کے ہاتھ میں ہلاک ہو گئی تو مشتری قیمت کا ضامن ہوگا۔ ر بائع نے تین دن کا خیار شرط لیا تھا اور مشتری نے بائع کی اجازت سے مبیع پر قبضہ کر لیا اور بعد میں مشتری کے ہاتھ میں طبع ہلاک ہوگئی تو جو من بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان طے ہوا تھا وہ تو لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن بازار میں اس طبیع کی جو قیمت ہوگی وہ ادا کرنا ہوگا۔ بائع کا خیار تھا اس لئے بائے کی ماکیت سے وہ چیز نہیں نکلی اور بیع بھی نہیں ہوئی لیکن مشتری نے بھاؤ کے طور پر وہ چیز لی تھی اور ہلاک ہوگئی اس لئے بازار کی جو قیمت ہوسکتی ہے وہ قیمت مشتری پر لازم ہوگی (۲) اس کا ثبوت اثر میں ہے۔ حضرت عمر نے ایک آدمی سے گھوڑا خریدا اگر پسند آئے گا تو رکھ لوں گا۔ پھر ایک آدمی کو اس پر سوار کیا جس کی وجہ سے گھوڑا عیب دار ہو گیا۔ حضرت عمر نے قاضی شریح کو فیصل مانا تو قاضی شریح نے فرمایا کہ آپ نے صحیح سالم لیا تھ اس لئے یاتو صیح سالم گھوڑا واپس کر دیا اس کی قیمت ادا کریں۔ فـقـال شريح لعمر اخذته صحيحا سليما وانت له ضامن حتى ترده صحيحا سليما (ب) (سنن بیھقی ، باب الماخوذ علی طریق السوم وعلی بیع شرط فيه الخيارج خامس ص۴۵۰، نمبر ۱۰۴۶۳ر مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الرجل یشتری الشی علی ان یحجر به فیهلک ج ثامن ص ۲۲۴ نمبر ۱۴۹۷۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا بیچ کر کے جدا نہ ہوں مگر رضا مندی کے بعد (ب) قاضی شریح نے حضرت عمر سے فرمایا آپ نے صحیح سالم گھوڑ الیا تھا اس لئے آپ اس کی قیمت کے ضامن ہیں یا یہ کہ اس کو صحیح سالم گھوڑا واپس کریں (نوٹ) اور صحیح سالم گھوڑ اواپس کر نہیں سکتے تو اس کی قیمت ادا کریں۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part Two, Book of Sales. Muhammad permits if a known period is specified. (850) (3) And the seller's option prevents the sold item from leaving his ownership. (851) (4) If the buyer takes possession and it perishes in his hand during the option period, he is liable for its value. There should be no problem, provided the period is known—how many days of option they want—not unknown. Their proof is the above hadith, which does not restrict to three days but gives option absolutely. (850) (3) The seller's option prevents the sold item from leaving his ownership. If the seller stipulates an option, even if the sold item has reached the buyer's hand, it is still in the seller's ownership; it has not left his ownership. When the seller chooses, it means that despite the sale, he still wants to keep it in his ownership. When he executes the sale, then the sold item will leave his ownership. This is why during this period, if he wants to free the sold item, he can free it, but the buyer cannot free it because the sold item has not yet entered his ownership. Thus, without the full consent of the seller, the sold item will not leave his hand. The hadith points to this: from Abu Hurairah from the Prophet (PBUH): 'Do not separate from a sale except with mutual consent' (Tirmidhi, chapter on khiyar al-mutabayi'in, p. 236, no. 1248; Abu Dawud, chapter on khiyar al-mutabayi'in, p. 133, no. 3358). This hadith states that seller and buyer should not separate without consent. Therefore, due to the stipulated option, the sale does not leave the seller's ownership. (851) (4) So if the buyer takes possession of the sold item and it perishes in his hand during the option period, the buyer is liable for its value. If the seller stipulated a three-day option and the buyer took possession with the seller's permission, and later the item perished in the buyer's hand, then the price agreed between seller and buyer is not binding. Rather, the market value of that item must be paid. The seller had the option, so the item did not leave his ownership and the sale did not occur. But the buyer took it as a trial and it perished, so the buyer is liable for the market value. The proof is in the athar: 'Umar bought a horse from a man with the condition: if I like it, I will keep it. Then he let a man ride it, causing a defect. 'Umar referred to Qadi Shurayh for judgment, and Shurayh said: 'You took it sound and healthy, so either return it sound and healthy or pay its value.' Shurayh said to 'Umar: 'You took it sound and healthy, and you are liable for it until you return it sound and healthy' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what is taken as a trial and on sale with option, vol. 5, p. 450, no. 10463; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on a man buying something with the condition to inspect it and it perishes, vol. 8, p. 224, no. 14979). From this athar it is understood that the buyer must pay the value because the sold item perished due to his action. Footnote (a): He said: 'Do not separate from a sale except after consent.' Footnote (b): Qadi Shurayh said to 'Umar: 'You took it sound and healthy, so you are liable for its value, or return it sound and healthy.' Note: And if you cannot return it sound and healthy, then pay its value.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the hadith and athar. The passage states that when a seller stipulates an option (khiyar al-shart) with a known period, the sold item remains in the seller's ownership during the option period. The authority of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani is cited: he permits the stipulation of a known period without restriction to three days, unlike Imam Abu Hanifa who limited it to three days. The proof is the hadith reported by Abu Hurairah: 'Do not separate from a sale except with mutual consent.' This hadith indicates that without full consent, the sale is not finalized. Therefore, if the seller has an option, his full consent is not yet given, so the sold item is not transferred. The passage then elaborates: even if the buyer takes possession, the item is still in the seller's ownership. The buyer cannot dispose of it (e.g., free a slave) because he is not the owner. The second part addresses a scenario where the buyer takes possession during the option period and the item perishes. The buyer is liable for the market value (qima) at the time of loss, not the agreed price, because the sale was not final. The proof is the athar of 'Umar and Shurayh: 'Umar took a horse on trial, caused a defect, and Shurayh ruled he was liable for the value. This establishes that whoever takes possession of a good on trial (bhaw) and it perishes is responsible for its value.

Key Terms
خيار البائع (khiyar al-ba'i'): The seller's right to cancel or confirm the sale within a stipulated period.
القيمة (al-qima): Market value of the sold item at the time of loss, not the agreed price.
الضمان (al-daman): Liability for compensation; here, the buyer must pay the market value because the item perished while in his possession under a trial arrangement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a seller stipulates a 5-day option for himself, and the buyer takes possession of the good, but the good perishes on day 3, what is the buyer liable for?
A) Nothing, because the sale is not finalized
B) The agreed price (thaman), because the sale becomes final upon loss
C) The market value (qima) of the good on the day it perished
D) Half the market value, because the seller still had the option

Key Takeaway
The seller's khiyar al-shart prevents ownership transfer; the buyer's possession does not imply ownership, and liability is based on market value if the item perishes.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Buyer's Khiyar al-Shart: Ownership During the Option Period
Explains the rule and intra-Hanafi dispute on whether ownership transfers to the buyer when buyer has option.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on ownership during buyer's khiyar al-shart and apply the mufta bihi ruling to cases of perishing or defect.

Core Idea
Buyer's option: ownership transfer disputed within Hanafi school; mufta bihi says it transfers.

When you buy a car with a 3-day return option, does the car become yours immediately? Hanafi scholars disagree. This lesson examines the rule and its practical consequences, focusing on the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and the dispute
State the basic rule: the buyer's option does not prevent the sold item from leaving the seller's ownership. Then identify the point of disagreement: does it enter the buyer's ownership during the option period?
The disagreement is between Abu Hanifa (no) and the Sahibayn (yes).
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Examine Abu Hanifa's reasoning: if the buyer owned the item immediately, buying a close relative (e.g., a brother) would cause automatic emancipation against the buyer's will. This shows ownership cannot transfer during the option.
This proof focuses on undesirable consequences.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
Understand the Sahibayn's qiyas: ownership cannot be in abeyance. Once the item leaves the seller's ownership, it must enter someone's; the only candidate is the buyer. Therefore, it enters his ownership.
This is a rational argument based on the nature of ownership.
4
Apply the mufta bihi to consequences
The relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn. If the item perishes or becomes defective in the buyer's hand, the sale becomes final and the buyer must pay the agreed price (thaman).
The loss or defect triggers the finalization of the sale.

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الثاني
۲۴
كتاب البيوع
[۸۵۲](۵) وخيار المشترى لا يمنع خروج المبيع من ملك البائع الا ان المشترى لا يملكه عند ابي حنيفة وقال ابو یوسف و محمد یملکه [۸۵۳] (۶) فان هلک بیده هلک بالثمن [۸۵۴] (۷) و کذلک ان دخله عيب.
کہ مشتری کو قیمت دینی ہوگی، کیونکہ اس کے کرتوت سے مبیع ہلاک ہوئی ہے۔ ۸۵۲ (۵) مشتری کا خیار شرط نہیں روکتا ہے بیچ کے نکلنے سے بائع کی ملکیت سے، مگر یہ کہ مشتری اس کا مالک نہیں ہوگا امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ مبیع کا مالک ہوگا۔
خیار شرط مشتری نے لیا ہے، بائع نے نہیں لیا ہے۔ اس لئے بائع نے تو اپنی جانب سے بیچ طے کر دی ہے اس لئے بائع کی ملکیت سے طبیع نکل جائے گی۔ لیکن مشتری نے خیار شرط لیا ہے تو گویا کہ مشتری نے ابھی مکمل بیچ طے نہیں کی اس لئے اس کی ملکیت میں مبیع داخل نہیں ہوگی۔ نیز اگر اس کی ملکیت میں داخل ہو جائے تو مشتری کا نقصان ہے۔ مثلا اگر اپنے بھائی کو خریدا تھا اور خیار شرطا لیا اس کے باوجود بھائی اس کی ملکیت میں داخل ہو گیا تو چونکہ وہ ذی رحم محرم ہے اس لئے بھائی آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اب مشتری کے نہ چاہتے ہوئے بھی بھائی آزاد ہو گیا۔ اس لئے امام ابوحنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مشتری کے خیار شرط کے وقت مبیع مشتری کی ملکیت میں داخل نہیں ہوگی۔ شمن : وہ ہے جو بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان قیمت طے ہو۔ قیمت : جو قیمت بازار میں لگ سکتی ہو اس کو قیمت کہتے ہیں۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ مشتری کی ملکیت میں داخل ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ بائع کی ملکیت سے نکل گئی تو مملوک شھی کسی نہ کسی کی ملکیت میں داخل ہونی چاہئے ورنہ وہ ملک کیسے ہوگی۔ اس لئے چاہے مشتری نے خیار لیا ہو پھر بھی اس کی ملکیت میں مبیع داخل ہو جائے گی۔
(۸۵۳ (۱) پس اگر مشتری کے ہاتھ میں ہلاک ہوگئی تو شمن کے بدلے میں ہلاک ہوگی۔
مشتری نے خیار شرط لیا اس لئے اس کی ملکیت میں داخل نہیں ہوئی تھی لیکن جب طبیع ہلاک ہونے لگی تو ہلاک ہونے سے پہلے وہ مشتری کی ملکیت میں داخل ہو گئی اور بیع مکمل ہو گئی۔ اور جب بیچ مکمل ہو گئی تو مشتری پر شمن لازم ہوگا ۔ یعنی وہ قیمت جو بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان طے ہوئی تھی۔ انوان بیع مکمل ہو گئی ہو تو شمن لازم ہوتا ہے۔
۸۵ (۷) ایسے ہی اگر مبیع میں عیب پیدا ہو گیا۔
یعنی مشتری نے خیار لیا تھا اور مبیع پر بھی قبضہ کیا تھا۔ مبیع مشتری کے ہاتھ میں رہتے ہوئے عیب دار ہو گئی تو بیع تام ہوگئی ۔ اس لئے مشتری کوشن دینا ہو گا جو آپس میں طے ہوا تھا۔ کیونکہ مشتری کے ہاتھ میں رہتے ہوئے بیع کے عیب دار ہونے سے بیع مکمل ہو جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ صبیح صحیح سالم لی تھی تو اب عیب دار کیسے واپس کرے گا۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part Two, p. 24, Book of Sales. (852) (5) And the buyer's option does not prevent the sold item from leaving the seller's ownership, except that the buyer does not own it according to Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said he owns it. (853) (6) If it perishes in his hand, it perishes against the price. (854) (7) Similarly, if a defect occurs. That the buyer must pay the value because the sold item perished due to his action. 852 (5) The buyer's stipulated option does not prevent the sale from leaving the seller's ownership, except that the buyer will not be the owner according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And the Sahibayn say he will be the owner. The option is taken by the buyer, not the seller. Therefore, the seller has finalized the sale from his side, so the sold item leaves the seller's ownership. But the buyer has taken an option, so it is as if the buyer has not yet finalized the sale; thus, the sold item does not enter his ownership. Also, if it were to enter his ownership, it would cause loss to the buyer. For example, if he bought his own brother and took an option, but despite that, the brother entered his ownership, then because he is a close relative (dhi rahm mahram), the brother would become free. So against the buyer's wish, the brother would be freed. Therefore, Imam Abu Hanifa says that during the buyer's option period, the sold item does not enter the buyer's ownership. Thaman: the price agreed between seller and buyer. Qima: the market value. The Sahibayn say it will enter the buyer's ownership because once it leaves the seller's ownership, it must enter someone's ownership; otherwise, it would be ownerless. So even if the buyer took an option, the sold item still enters his ownership. (853) (1) Then if it perishes in the buyer's hand, it perishes against the price. The buyer took an option, so it had not entered his ownership, but when the sold item begins to perish, before perishing it enters the buyer's ownership and the sale becomes complete. And when the sale is complete, the buyer owes the price, i.e., the price agreed between seller and buyer. Because if the sale becomes complete, the price becomes due. (854) (7) Similarly, if a defect occurs in the sold item. That is, the buyer had taken an option and had taken possession of the sold item. While the sold item was in the buyer's hand, it became defective. Then the sale becomes complete. Therefore, the buyer must pay the price that was agreed. Because while it was in his hand, the sold item becoming defective completes the sale. Since he took it sound and healthy, how can he return it defective?
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the buyer's khiyar al-shart. The passage presents the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad). The central issue is whether the sold item enters the buyer's ownership during the option period when the buyer has stipulated the option. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the sold item does not become the buyer's property during the option period because the buyer's consent is not yet final. The proof is practical: if the buyer were to own the item, then buying a relative (like a brother) would result in automatic emancipation, causing loss to the buyer against his will. The Sahibayn argue that ownership must transfer to someone; otherwise, the item would become ownerless. Therefore, it enters the buyer's ownership. The passage then discusses consequences: if the good perishes in the buyer's hand, according to the Sahibayn, it perishes against the price (thaman), meaning the buyer must pay the agreed price because the sale is considered finalized at the moment of loss (or defect). Similarly, if a defect occurs in the good, the sale becomes final and the buyer must pay the price. The commentary clarifies that thaman is the agreed price, while qima is market value. The ruling aligns with the Sahibayn's view that upon loss or defect, the sale is complete and the buyer owes the price. This is the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
خيار المشترى (khiyar al-mushtari): The buyer's right to cancel or confirm the sale within a stipulated period.
ثمن (thaman): The agreed price between buyer and seller.
قيمة (qima): Market value of the item, used when the sale is not finalized (e.g., seller's option).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, what happens to the sold item during the buyer's option period?
A) It remains in the seller's ownership.
B) It enters the buyer's ownership.
C) It becomes ownerless until the option is exercised.
D) It is jointly owned by both parties.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi mufta bihi, the buyer owns during his option period; loss or defect finalizes the sale and the buyer pays the agreed price.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Buyer's Option and Ownership During Khiyar al-Shart: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Ruling on buyer's option and its effect on ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's position on ownership during khiyar al-shart, explain the Sahibayn's counter-argument, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of this intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
When a buyer holds an option, ownership is suspended to prevent harm—Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn insist ownership must transfer immediately.

When a buyer stipulates an option (khiyar al-shart), does he immediately own the purchased item? This seemingly technical question has significant practical consequences. Within the Hanafi school, Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), disagreed. This lesson unpacks both positions, their proofs, and the real-world impact on liability, using the example of purchasing a mahram relative.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position
Identify what Abu Hanifa holds: the sold item leaves the seller's ownership but does not enter the buyer's ownership during the option period.
This is a unique third state—ownership is suspended.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's opposing view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the sold item enters the buyer's ownership immediately, because ownership cannot be in limbo.
They argue the item must be owned by someone.
3
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
Their reasoning: since the item left the seller's ownership, it must transfer to another owner; the only candidate is the buyer.
This is a logical necessity argument.
4
Analyse Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa invokes the principle of preventing harm (daf' al-darar). If ownership transferred immediately, the buyer could suffer loss—e.g., if the item is a mahram relative who would become free upon purchase, regardless of the buyer's wish to cancel.
This practical harm outweighs the need for immediate assignment of ownership.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the sold item is destroyed or a defect occurs during the option period, under Abu Hanifa the buyer is not liable (he is not owner); under the Sahibayn the buyer is liable as owner.
Also affects liability for price and ability to sell the item during the option.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخيار المشترى لا يمنع خروج المبيع من ملك البائع الا ان المشترى لا يملكه عند ابي حنيفة وقال ابو يوسف و محمد يملکه

مشتری کا خیار شرط نہیں روکتا ہے بیچ کے نکلنے سے بائع کی ملکیت سے، مگر یہ کہ مشتری اس کا مالک نہیں ہوگا امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ مبیع کا مالک ہوگا۔ خیار شرط مشتری نے لیا ہے، بائع نے نہیں لیا ہے۔ اس لئے بائع نے تو اپنی جانب سے بیچ طے کر دی ہے اس لئے بائع کی ملکیت سے طبیع نکل جائے گی۔ لیکن مشتری نے خیار شرط لیا ہے تو گویا کہ مشتری نے ابھی مکمل بیچ طے نہیں کی اس لئے اس کی ملکیت میں مبیع داخل نہیں ہوگی۔ نیز اگر اس کی ملکیت میں داخل ہو جائے تو مشتری کا نقصان ہے۔ مثلا اگر اپنے بھائی کو خریدا تھا اور خیار شرطا لیا اس کے باوجود بھائی اس کی ملکیت میں داخل ہو گیا تو چونکہ وہ ذی رحم محرم ہے اس لئے بھائی آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اب مشتری کے نہ چاہتے ہوئے بھی بھائی آزاد ہو گیا۔ اس لئے امام ابوحنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مشتری کے خیار شرط کے وقت مبیع مشتری کی ملکیت میں داخل نہیں ہوگی۔ شمن : وہ ہے جو بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان قیمت طے ہو۔ قیمت : جو قیمت بازار میں لگ سکتی ہو اس کو قیمت کہتے ہیں۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ مشتری کی ملکیت میں داخل ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ بائع کی ملکیت سے نکل گئی تو مملوک شھی کسی نہ کسی کی ملکیت میں داخل ہونی چاہئے ورنہ وہ ملک کیسے ہوگی۔ اس لئے چاہے مشتری نے خیار لیا ہو پھر بھی اس کی ملکیت میں مبیع داخل ہو جائے گی۔
The buyer's option does not prevent the sold item from leaving the ownership of the seller, except that the buyer does not own it according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: he owns it. / The buyer's khiyar al-shart does not prevent the sale from leaving the seller's ownership, except that the buyer will not be its owner according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And the Sahibayn say: the sold item will be owned by the buyer. The khiyar al-shart was taken by the buyer, not the seller. Therefore, the seller has finalized the sale from his side, so the sold item will leave the seller's ownership. But the buyer has taken the option, so as if the buyer has not yet fully finalized the sale, so the sold item does not enter his ownership. Also, if it entered his ownership, there would be a loss for the buyer. For example, if he bought his brother and took the option, and despite that the brother entered his ownership, then since the brother is a mahram relative, the brother would become free. So even if the buyer does not want it, the brother becomes free. Therefore, Imam Abu Hanifa says: at the time of the buyer's khiyar al-shart, the sold item does not enter the buyer's ownership. Thaman: the price agreed upon between seller and buyer. Qimah: the market price. The Sahibayn say: it will enter the buyer's ownership. Because it left the seller's ownership, so the owned thing must enter someone's ownership, otherwise how would it be owned? Therefore, even if the buyer took the option, the sold item still enters his ownership.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the effect of khiyar al-shart (option of condition) when it is granted to the buyer. The ruling states that the buyer's option does not prevent the sold item from leaving the seller's ownership, but the buyer does not own it according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree, holding that the buyer does own it. The commentary explains Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the seller has finalized the sale unconditionally, so ownership leaves him, but the buyer's option indicates incomplete consent, so ownership does not transfer. An example illustrates the practical consequence: if the buyer purchases a relative who is a mahram (like a brother), and the condition is that the buyer has an option, then if ownership transferred immediately, the brother would become free upon purchase, causing harm to the buyer. To prevent this harm, Abu Hanifa delays ownership until the option period ends or the sale is confirmed. The Sahibayn argue that since ownership has left the seller, it must belong to someone; it cannot be in limbo, so it transfers to the buyer despite the option. The passage also clarifies terms: 'thaman' is the contract price agreed upon, while 'qimah' is the market price. This distinction is important for later rulings on liability.

Key Terms
خیار شرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in the contract allowing one party to confirm or cancel the sale within a specified period.
ثمن (thaman): The specific price agreed upon by the buyer and seller in the contract.
قیمت (qimah): The market price or value of an item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when a buyer has khiyar al-shart, does the sold item enter the buyer's ownership?
A) Yes, immediately
B) No, it remains in the seller's ownership
C) No, it does not enter the buyer's ownership
D) It depends on the type of option

Key Takeaway
During khiyar al-shart held by the buyer, ownership is suspended according to Abu Hanifa, while the Sahibayn hold it transfers; the practical difference is liability for loss.
