Liability for Destruction or Defect During Buyer's Option
Ruling on liability when sold item perishes or develops defect during buyer's option

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when the sold item perishes or becomes defective during the buyer's khiyar al-shart, explain the legal mechanism of retroactive ownership, and apply the principle to similar scenarios.

Core Idea
During the buyer's option, possession creates liability: destruction or defect finalizes the sale and obligates the price.

This passage addresses a critical question in sales law: if the buyer takes possession of an item under an option (khiyar al-shart) and the item is destroyed or develops a defect, who bears the loss? The Hanafi school provides a clear answer grounded in a subtle legal mechanism and a companion's precedent. Understanding this ruling is essential for both jurists and practitioners dealing with conditional sales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the outcome when the sold item perishes or a defect occurs in the buyer's hand during khiyar al-shart.
The matn says: 'If it perishes in his hand, it perishes with the price. Similarly, if a defect occurs.'
2
Understand the legal mechanism
Explain why the sale becomes complete at the moment of destruction or defect. The commentary notes that ownership transfers retroactively just before the loss, making the buyer liable.
This prevents the buyer from having both the option and escaping liability for damage he caused.
3
Examine the proof
Analyze Qadi Shurayh's statement to Caliph Umar: 'You took it sound and intact, so you are a guarantor for it until you return it sound and intact.' Understand how this serves as a precedent (qawl sahabi) for the ruling.
The dalil is a statement of a companion, which is a source in Hanafi usul.
4
Apply to a parallel case
Consider a modern scenario: a buyer takes a phone on a 7-day return policy and accidentally cracks the screen. Apply the ruling: the sale becomes complete, and the buyer must pay the full price.
This demonstrates the strict liability of the buyer once he takes possession during the option.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان هلک بیده هلک بالثمن و کذلک ان دخله عيب

پس اگر مشتری کے ہاتھ میں ہلاک ہوگئی تو شمن کے بدلے میں ہلاک ہوگی۔
مشتری نے خیار شرط لیا اس لئے اس کی ملکیت میں داخل نہیں ہوئی تھی لیکن جب طبیع ہلاک ہونے لگی تو ہلاک ہونے سے پہلے وہ مشتری کی ملکیت میں داخل ہو گئی اور بیع مکمل ہو گئی۔ اور جب بیچ مکمل ہو گئی تو مشتری پر شمن لازم ہوگا ۔ یعنی وہ قیمت جو بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان طے ہوئی تھی۔ انوان بیع مکمل ہو گئی ہو تو شمن لازم ہوتا ہے۔
مثلًا اگر مبیع میں عیب پیدا ہو گیا۔
یعنی مشتری نے خیار لیا تھا اور مبیع پر بھی قبضہ کیا تھا۔ مبیع مشتری کے ہاتھ میں رہتے ہوئے عیب دار ہو گئی تو بیع تام ہوگئی ۔ اس لئے مشتری کوشن دینا ہو گا جو آپس میں طے ہوا تھا۔ کیونکہ مشتری کے ہاتھ میں رہتے ہوئے بیع کے عیب دار ہونے سے بیع مکمل ہو جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ صبیح صحیح سالم لی تھی تو اب عیب دار کیسے واپس کرے گا۔
مسئلہ نمبرہ میں قاضی شریح کا جملہ گزرا فقال شريح لـعـمـر اخذته صحيحا سليما وانت له ضامن حتى ترده صحيحا سليما (الف) (سنن سبیھقی ، باب الماخوذ علی طریق السوم و علی بیع شرط فیه خیار ج خامس ص ۴۵۰ نمبر ۱۰۴۶۳ر مصنف عبدالرزاق نمبر ۱۴۹۷۹) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مشتری کے ہاتھ میں مبیع عیب دار ہو جائے تو اس کو اس کی قیمت دینی ہوگی اور مبیع مشتری کی ہوگی اور بیچ تام ہو جائے گی۔
If it perishes in his hand, it perishes with the price. Similarly, if a defect occurs in it. / So if it perishes in the buyer's hand, it perishes in exchange for the price. The buyer took the option, so it had not entered his ownership, but when the sold item began to perish, before perishing it entered the buyer's ownership and the sale became complete. And when the sale is complete, the buyer is liable for the price, i.e., the price agreed upon between seller and buyer. For example, if a defect occurs in the sold item. That is, the buyer had taken the option and had taken possession of the sold item. While in the buyer's hand, it became defective, so the sale becomes complete. Therefore, the buyer must pay the agreed price. Because when the buyer took it sound and intact, how can he return it defective? In the previous issue, the statement of Qadi Shurayh passed: he said to Umar, 'You took it sound and intact, so you are a guarantor for it until you return it sound and intact.' From this it is understood that if the sold item becomes defective in the buyer's hand, he must pay its price, the sold item becomes his, and the sale is complete.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage builds on the previous ruling. It presents the legal consequence of destruction or defect during the buyer's option period. The matn states: if the sold item perishes in the buyer's hand, it perishes with the price, meaning the buyer is liable. Similarly, if a defect occurs. The commentary explains the mechanism: although the buyer had an option and did not initially own the item, at the moment of destruction (or defect), the sale becomes complete and ownership transfers to the buyer just before the loss, making him liable for the price. This is to prevent the buyer from having both the option and escaping liability for damage he caused. The same applies if a defect occurs: since the buyer received the item sound, his inability to return it sound leads to the sale being finalized. The commentary also cites a historical precedent: Qadi Shurayh told Caliph Umar that he was a guarantor for a horse he took sound and must return it sound. This serves as a proof (qawl sahabi) for the ruling. The hadith from Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq is referenced to support the principle that the buyer is liable for defects occurring in his possession. This shows that even during the option period, the buyer is considered a guarantor (damin) for the sold item, and any damage or defect results in his liability and completion of the sale.

Key Terms
هلک بالثمن (halaka bi al-thaman): The sold item perishes in exchange for the price, meaning the buyer must pay the price.
ضامن (damin): Guarantor; one who is liable for compensation if the item is damaged or lost.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the sold item perishes in the buyer's hand during his khiyar al-shart?
A) The buyer cancels the sale and pays nothing
B) The sale is canceled and the seller bears the loss
C) The sale becomes complete and the buyer must pay the price
D) The buyer returns the item and pays half price

Key Takeaway
If the sold item perishes or becomes defective in the buyer's hand during khiyar al-shart, the sale is finalized and the buyer must pay the full price.

Cancellation in Khiyar al-Shart: Presence Requirement to Prevent Harm
Ruling on khiyar al-shart: confirmation and cancellation conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cancellation during khiyar al-shart, explain the condition of presence, and apply the hadith 'la darar' to justify the requirement.

Core Idea
Cancellation during khiyar al-shart is invalid without the other party's presence to prevent harm.

When a party has a stipulated option (khiyar al-shart), he may confirm or cancel the sale. However, the Hanafi school distinguishes between confirmation and cancellation: confirmation causes no harm and is valid even in absence, but cancellation can harm the other party who relied on the sale. Therefore, cancellation requires the other party to be present or informed. This ruling is grounded in the prophetic maxim 'La darar wa la dirar' (no harm and no reciprocation of harm).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What are the two acts the option-holder can perform? Confirmation (ijaza) and cancellation (faskh). What is the ruling for each when the other party is absent?
Confirmation is valid in absence; cancellation is not.
2
Locate the condition for cancellation
The passage states cancellation is not valid 'unless the other is present.' Identify the condition: presence (or notification) of the other party.
This condition applies only to cancellation, not confirmation.
3
Examine the proof
The hadith 'La darar wa la dirar' is cited. How does it support the condition? Cancelling without notice causes harm (darar) to the other party, which is prohibited.
The hadith is a general principle used here to justify the ruling.
4
Analyze the intra-madhhab dispute
Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i allow cancellation even in absence. What is their argument? The option-holder has full authority, so he may cancel unilaterally, just as he can confirm.
The Hanafi response: cancellation causes harm, unlike confirmation.
5
Determine the practical consequence
What is the thamarah al-khilaf? Under the Hanafi view, the other party is protected from loss; under the opposing view, the option-holder has more flexibility.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position requiring presence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن شرط له الخيار فله ان يسفخ فى مدة الخيار وله ان يجيزه فان اجازه بغير حضرة صاحبه جاز وان فسخ لم يجز الا ان يكون الآخر حاضرا

جس نے خیار شرط لیا اس کے لئے جائز ہے کہ مدت خیار میں بیچ فسخ کر دے اور اس کے لئے یہ بھی جائز ہے کہ اس کو جائز کر دے۔
چونکہ اس نے بیع جائز قرار دینے اور بیچ کے توڑنے کا اختیار لیا ہے اس لئے اس کو دونوں اختیار ہیں ۔ چاہے تو تین دن کے اندر بیج توڑ دے، چاہے تو جائز قرار دے۔
پس اگر سامنے والے کی غیر حاضری میں بیع جائز قرار دی تو جائز ہے، اور اگر بیچ فسخ کی تو جائز نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ دوسرا حاضر ہو
مثلا بائع نے خیار شرط لیا تو مشتری سامنے نہ بھی ہو یا اس کو علم نہ بھی ہو تب بھی بیع جائز قرار دینا چاہے تو جائز قرادے سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ بیع جائز قرار دینے میں مشتری کا نقصان نہیں ہے وہ تو چاہ ہی رہا ہے کہ بیچ جائز ہو جائے تب ہی تو اس نے خیار شرط نہیں لیا۔ اس لئے مشتری کو علم نہ بھی ہوا ہوتب بھی بیع جائز قرار دے سکتا ہے۔ اور اگر بائع بیچ فسخ کرنا چاہتا ہو تو جب تک مشتری کو اس کی خبر نہ دے شیخ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مشتری کو فسخ کرنے سے نقصان ہوگا۔ وہ سمجھ رہا تھا کہ بیع جائز کردیگا لیکن اس نے فسخ کر دیا۔ اب اس نے دوسری طبیع تلاش نہیں کی اور انتظار میں بیٹھا رہا۔ اس لئے اگر فتح کرنا ہو تو دوسرے فریق کو اس کی اطلاع دینا ضروری ہے۔ تا کہ اس کو نقصان نہ ہو (۲) حدیث میں اس کی تصریح ہے عن عائشة عن النبی الا الله قال لا ضرر ولا ضرار (ب) (دار قطنی، كتاب في الاقضية والاحکام ج رابع ص ۱۴۶ نمبر ۳۰۶۰/۴۴۹۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کسی کو نقصان دینے سے بچنا چاہئے۔
امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ دوسرے فریق کو اطلاع دیئے بغیر بھی فسخ کرنا چاہے تو کر سکتا ہے۔ دوسرے فریق نے اختیار لینے والے کو بیع توڑنے کا بھی اختیار دیا ہے اس لئے وہ جس طرح غائبانہ میں بیع جائز قرار دے سکتا ہے اسی طرح تو ڑ بھی سکتا ہے۔ ات الا ان يكون الحاضر کا مطلب یہ نہیں ہے کہ دوسرا فریق حاضر ہو بلکہ اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ چاہے وہ حاضر نہ ہولیکن اس کو بیع ضح حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت قاضی شریح نے حضرت عمر سے فرمایا کہ آپ نے گھوڑے کو صحیح سالم لیا اس لئے آپ ضامن ہیں۔ یہاں تک کہ اس کو صحیح سالم واپس کریں (ب) آپ نے فرمایا نہ نقصان اٹھانا چاہئے اور نہ نقصان دینا چاہئے
And whoever is given the option may cancel within the option period and may confirm it. If he confirms it in the absence of the other party, it is valid; and if he cancels, it is not valid unless the other is present. / Whoever takes the option, it is permissible for him to cancel the sale during the option period and it is also permissible for him to confirm it. Since he has taken the authority to confirm or cancel the sale, he has both options. He may break the sale within three days or confirm it. So if he confirms the sale in the absence of the other party, it is valid; and if he cancels, it is not valid unless the other is present. For example, if the seller took the option, then even if the buyer is not present or unaware, the seller may confirm the sale if he wishes. Because in confirming there is no loss for the buyer, he wants the sale to be confirmed anyway (since he did not take the option). Therefore, even if the buyer does not know, confirmation is valid. But if the seller wants to cancel, he cannot do so unless the buyer is informed. Because cancellation would harm the buyer, as he may have relied on the sale and not sought other goods. Therefore, if cancellation is desired, the other party must be informed to prevent harm. (2) The hadith clarifies this: from Aisha from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said, 'There is no harm and no reciprocation of harm.' (Dar Qutni) This hadith shows that one must avoid causing harm to others. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Shafi'i say that cancellation is valid even without informing the other party. Because the party gave the option-holder the right to break the sale, so he may do so in absence just as he can confirm in absence. The meaning of 'unless the other is present' is not that the other party must be physically present, but that even if he is not present, the cancellation is valid. (Footnotes: (a) Qadi Shurayh told Umar: 'You took it sound and intact, so you are a guarantor until you return it sound.' (b) The Prophet said: 'Do not cause harm nor reciprocate harm.')
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on exercising khiyar al-shart. The option-holder has the right to either confirm (ijaza) or cancel (faskh) the sale during the option period. However, there is a key condition regarding cancellation: if the option-holder wants to cancel, the other party must be present (or at least informed), because cancellation causes loss to the other party who may have relied on the sale. In contrast, confirmation does not cause harm, so it can be done even in the other party's absence. The commentary illustrates with an example: if the seller has the option, he can confirm the sale even if the buyer is absent, but cannot cancel without informing the buyer. The hadith 'La darar wa la dirar' (no harm and no reciprocation of harm) from Dar Qutni is cited as a proof. The passage also records a disagreement: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that cancellation is also valid in absence, arguing that the option-holder has full authority over the sale. The Hanafi position (apparently following Abu Hanifa) insists on notification to prevent harm. This lesson highlights the principle that concepts like darar (harm) are central to Hanafi rulings on khiyar.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Cancellation or annulment of the contract, one of the options available to the option-holder.
إجازة (ijaza): Confirmation or ratification of the contract, making it binding.
لا ضرر ولا ضرار (la darar wa la dirar): A legal maxim meaning 'no harm and no reciprocation of harm,' used to justify rulings that prevent injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, can the option-holder cancel the sale without the other party being present?
A) Yes, any time
B) No, unless the other party is present or informed
C) Only if the option is for the seller
D) Only if the sale is a sale of currency (sarf)

Key Takeaway
Cancellation in khiyar al-shart requires the other party's presence or notification to prevent harm, based on the hadith 'la darar'.

Khiyar al-Shart: Option to Confirm or Cancel
Ruling on khiyar al-shart's options

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of khiyar al-shart and explain the option-holder's discretion to cancel or confirm the sale.

Core Idea
The option-holder may freely cancel or confirm the sale within the stipulated period.

In this passage, the author of Al-Sharh al-Saghir states the core ruling of khiyar al-shart: the party with the option has full discretion to cancel or affirm the sale. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its implications, including the additional point about liability during the option period as illustrated by Qadi Sharih's ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is khiyar al-shart (option of condition). The ruling is that the option-holder may either cancel (yufsikh) or confirm (yujizu) the sale during the option period.
The Arabic matn uses 'yufsikh' and 'yujizu'.
2
Note the scope of discretion
The option-holder has absolute discretion; no specific reason is required for cancellation or confirmation. Both actions are equally permissible (ja'iz).
This is a right, not an obligation.
3
Connect to the default period
If no period is specified, the default is three days. The option expires after the agreed period, and the sale becomes binding upon confirmation or expiry without cancellation.
The text does not specify the period but commentary implies three days.
4
Understand the legal consequence
If confirmed, the sale is binding and ownership transfers retrospectively. If cancelled, the sale is void, and the parties return to pre-contract status.
Liability for damage during the option period is on the buyer (as per Qadi Sharih).
5
Review the supporting evidence
The text cites Qadi Sharih's statement to 'Umar: the buyer is a guarantor until the item is returned sound. This shows that during the option period, risk lies with the buyer, reinforcing the binding nature of the sale upon confirmation.
The evidence is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۸۵۵] (۸) ومن شرط له الخيار فله ان يسفخ فى مدة الخيار وله ان يجيزه مسئلہ نمبرہ میں قاضی شریح کا جملہ گزرا فقال شريح لـعـمـر اخذته صحيحا سليما وانت له ضامن حتى ترده صحيحا سليما (الف) (سنن سبیھقی ، باب الماخوذ علی طریق السوم و علی بیع شرط فیه خیار ج خامس ص ۴۵۰ نمبر ۱۰۴۶۳ر مصنف عبدالرزاق نمبر ۱۴۹۷۹) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مشتری کے ہاتھ میں مبیع عیب دار ہو جائے تو اس کو اس کی قیمت دینی ہوگی اور مبیع مشتری کی ہوگی اور بیچ تام ہو جائے گی۔ [۸۵۵] (۸) جس نے خیار شرط لیا اس کے لئے جائز ہے کہ مدت خیار میں بیچ فسخ کر دے اور اس کے لئے یہ بھی جائز ہے کہ اس کو جائز کر دے۔ چونکہ اس نے بیع جائز قرار دینے اور بیچ کے توڑنے کا اختیار لیا ہے اس لئے اس کو دونوں اختیار ہیں ۔ چاہے تو تین دن کے اندر بیج توڑ دے، چاہے تو جائز قرار دے۔
[855] (8) And whoever stipulates an option for himself, he may cancel during the period of the option, and he may confirm it. In issue number, the statement of Qadi Sharih passed: He said to 'Umar: 'You took it sound and safe, and you are a guarantor for it until you return it sound and safe.' (From Sunan al-Bayhaqi, etc.) From this it is understood that if the commodity becomes defective in the buyer's hand, then he must pay its price, and the commodity is the buyer's, and the sale becomes complete. [855] (8) Whoever stipulates an option for himself, it is permissible for him to cancel the sale during the option period, and it is also permissible for him to confirm it. Since he has taken the authority to confirm and cancel, he has both options. He may cancel within three days or confirm.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on khiyar al-shart (option of condition). The text first quotes the Arabic matn: 'Whoever stipulates an option for himself may cancel during the option period or confirm.' The commentary then provides supporting evidence from Qadi Sharih's statement to 'Umar regarding liability for a defective horse taken on approval, indicating that if the buyer damages the item, he must pay its value. This is connected because the option period does not transfer ownership completely until confirmation. The Urdu sharh explains that since the person stipulated the option, he has both authorities: to cancel or to confirm the sale within the three-day period typical for khiyar al-shart. The ruling is straightforward: the option-holder has full discretion.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in a sale contract that gives one or both parties the right to cancel or confirm within a specified period (usually three days).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does khiyar al-shart allow the option-holder to do?
A) Only confirm the sale
B) Only cancel the sale
C) Either confirm or cancel the sale within the option period
D) Demand a lower price

Key Takeaway
The option-holder has full discretion to cancel or confirm the sale within the stipulated period.

Confirmation and Cancellation in Absence
Ruling on confirmation and cancellation in absence with khiyar al-shart

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between confirmation and cancellation of a sale with khiyar al-shart when the other party is absent, and state the Hanafi ruling with its dalil.

Core Idea
Confirmation benefits; cancellation harms. The rule: no harm prevents cancellation without notice.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario in sales with options (khiyar al-shart): can the option-holder confirm or cancel the sale when the other party is not present? The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the impact on the other party, applying the prophetic maxim 'La darar wa la dirar' (No harm and no reciprocating harm). Understanding this distinction is key to grasping how Hanafi fiqh balances contractual freedom with the prevention of harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Name the act (confirmation or cancellation of a sale with khiyar al-shart) and state the Hanafi ruling for each when the other party is absent.
Confirmation is valid; cancellation is invalid without the other party's presence or notice.
2
Understand the rationale
Analyze why the ruling differs: confirmation benefits the buyer (he wants the sale), while cancellation harms him (he expected confirmation and may have missed other opportunities).
The principle of preventing harm (darar) justifies the distinction.
3
Examine the dalil
Identify the hadith 'La darar wa la dirar' and explain how it supports the ruling: cancellation without notice causes harm, which is prohibited.
The dalil is ahad but its meaning is clear and authoritative.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf
Compare the positions of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i, who hold that cancellation is also valid in absence, and evaluate the Hanafi response.
The Hanafi response relies on the overriding importance of preventing harm over the general authority of the option-holder.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۸۵۶] (۹) فان اجازه بغير حضرة صاحبه جاز وان فسخ لم يجز الا ان يكون الآخر حاضرا. پس اگر سامنے والے کی غیر حاضری میں بیع جائز قرار دی تو جائز ہے، اور اگر بیچ فسخ کی تو جائز نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ دوسرا حاضر ہو مثلا بائع نے خیار شرط لیا تو مشتری سامنے نہ بھی ہو یا اس کو علم نہ بھی ہو تب بھی بیع جائز قرار دینا چاہے تو جائز قرادے سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ بیع جائز قرار دینے میں مشتری کا نقصان نہیں ہے وہ تو چاہ ہی رہا ہے کہ بیچ جائز ہو جائے تب ہی تو اس نے خیار شرط نہیں لیا۔ اس لئے مشتری کو علم نہ بھی ہوا ہوتب بھی بیع جائز قرار دے سکتا ہے۔ اور اگر بائع بیچ فسخ کرنا چاہتا ہو تو جب تک مشتری کو اس کی خبر نہ دے شیخ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مشتری کو فسخ کرنے سے نقصان ہوگا۔ وہ سمجھ رہا تھا کہ بیع جائز کردیگا لیکن اس نے فسخ کر دیا۔ اب اس نے دوسری طبیع تلاش نہیں کی اور انتظار میں بیٹھا رہا۔ اس لئے اگر فتح کرنا ہو تو دوسرے فریق کو اس کی اطلاع دینا ضروری ہے۔ تا کہ اس کو نقصان نہ ہو (۲) حدیث میں اس کی تصریح ہے عن عائشة عن النبی الا الله قال لا ضرر ولا ضرار (ب) (دار قطنی، كتاب في الاقضية والاحکام ج رابع ص ۱۴۶ نمبر ۳۰۶۰/۴۴۹۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کسی کو نقصان دینے سے بچنا چاہئے۔ امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ دوسرے فریق کو اطلاع دیئے بغیر بھی فسخ کرنا چاہے تو کر سکتا ہے۔ دوسرے فریق نے اختیار لینے والے کو بیع توڑنے کا بھی اختیار دیا ہے اس لئے وہ جس طرح غائبانہ میں بیع جائز قرار دے سکتا ہے اسی طرح توڑ بھی سکتا ہے۔
[856] (9) If he confirms the sale without the presence of the other party, it is valid; but if he cancels, it is not valid unless the other is present. So if the seller stipulated the option, even if the buyer is not present or unaware, he can confirm the sale validly. Because confirmation causes no harm to the buyer—in fact, he wants the sale to be confirmed; that is why he did not stipulate the option. So even if the buyer is unaware, the seller can confirm. But if the seller wants to cancel the sale, it is not valid until he informs the buyer. Because cancellation harms the buyer; he was expecting confirmation and may not have sought another buyer. Therefore cancellation requires informing the other party to avoid harm. The hadith clarifies: 'La darar wa la dirar' (No harm and no reciprocating harm). From this we learn to avoid causing harm. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i say that cancellation is valid even without informing the other party because the option-holder has been given the authority to cancel, just as he can confirm in absence.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and an intra- and inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa) distinguishes between confirmation and cancellation when the other party is absent: confirmation is valid because it benefits the other party or at least does him no harm; cancellation is invalid without the other party's presence or knowledge because it causes harm, which is prohibited by the hadith 'La darar wa la dirar' (No harm and no reciprocating harm). Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i argue that cancellation should also be valid in absence since the option-holder has full authority. The Hanafi response relies on the principle of preventing harm: cancellation without notice leaves the other party at a disadvantage, so it is not permitted. The commentator explains that this is a practical application of the legal maxim 'Harm must be removed' (al-darar yuzal).

Key Terms
لا ضرر ولا ضرار (la darar wa la dirar): A prophetic hadith meaning 'No harm and no reciprocating harm,' used as a legal maxim in Hanafi fiqh to prohibit causing harm to others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is cancellation of a sale with khiyar al-shart invalid in the absence of the other party without informing him?
A) Because the option period has expired
B) Because it causes harm to the other party
C) Because the option-holder lacks authority
D) Because the sale was not confirmed initially

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, cancellation of a sale with khiyar al-shart without informing the other party is invalid due to the principle 'no harm'.

Sale with Defective Description: Buyer's Option
Ruling that if a sold item lacks a described quality, the buyer has the option to take or return.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the buyer's options when a sold item lacks a described quality and explain the Hanafi rule that no price reduction is permitted.

Core Idea
The buyer's option is binary: take at full price or return; no reduction for a missing quality.

When a seller explicitly describes a specific quality (e.g., a slave is a baker) and that quality is absent, the buyer is not left without recourse. However, the Hanafi school gives a clear, limited remedy: either accept the item at the full agreed price or return it. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this rule and the hadith that supports it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a sale where the seller explicitly describes a quality. The ruling gives the buyer an option (khiyar) if that quality is missing.
This is not a defect in the item itself but a missing described attribute.
2
Understand the buyer's two options
The buyer may either keep the item by paying the full price or return it. No third option (like a reduced price) exists by default.
A price reduction would require a new agreement with the seller.
3
Analyze the basis for the rule
The rule derives from the hadith 'When you sell, say: no deception.' The command implies that deception (like a false description) gives the buyer a right to annul.
This hadith is ahad, so its dalala is zanni, but it is sufficient for establishing a khiyar.
4
Apply to other sale items
The ruling applies to any sold item with an expressly stated quality, not just slaves. For example, a car described as having a sunroof.
The quality must be explicitly mentioned; implied qualities are not covered.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۸۵۸] (۱۱) ومن باع غلاما على انه خباز او كاتب فوجده على خلاف ذلك فللمشترى ان يأخذه بجميع الثمن وان يتركه. کسی نے غلام بیچا یہ کہ کر کہ یہ روٹی پکانے والا یا کاتب ہے پس اس کو اس کے خلاف پایا تو مشتری کو اس کا اختیار ہے کہ اگر چا ہے تو پوراشن دے کر لے اور اگر چاہے تو اس کو چھوڑ دے۔ غلام بیچا یہ کہہ کر کہ یہ روٹی پکانے والا ہے لیکن بعد میں پتہ چلا کہ وہ صفت اس غلام میں نہیں ہے تو اس صفت کے نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے مشتری کو بیع جائز قرار دینے اور بیچ کے توڑنے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ صفت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کی رغبت کم ہوگئی اور بائع نے خلاف وعدہ کیا اس لئے اس کو توڑنے کا حق ہو گا۔ اور اگر غلام لینا چاہے تو جو قیمت آپس میں طے ہوئی تھی وہی قیمت دے کر لینا ہوگا۔ روٹی پکانا کاتب ہونا یہ صفت ہے اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ صفت کے مقابلے میں مستقل قیمت نہیں ہوتی اس لئے اس صفت کی کمی کی وجہ سے قیمت میں کمی نہیں ہوگی۔ وت ہاں ! بائع قیمت کم کرنے پر راضی ہو جائے تو گویا کہ الگ صفقہ کے ماتحت کم ہوئی جس کی گنجائش ہے۔ البتہ قانونی طور پر پہلی ہی قیمت میں لینا ہوگا۔ اس کا ثبوت حدیث سے ملتا ہے عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رجلا ذكر للنبى الله انه يخدع في البيوع فقال اذا بايعت فقل لا خلابة (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب ما يكره من الخداع في البيع ص ۲۸۴ نمبر ۲۱۱۷ / ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فیمن سخدع فی حاشیہ : (الف) آپ کے سامنے تذکرہ آیا کہ ایک آدمی بیچ میں دھو کہ کھا جاتا ہے تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ جب آپ بیچ کریں تو کہہ دیا کریں کہ دھوکہ نہیں (نوٹ) دوسری حدیث میں آپ کو تین دن کا اختیار لینے کو فرمایا تھا )
[858] (11) And whoever sells a slave on the condition that he is a bread-maker or a scribe, and then finds him contrary to that, then the buyer has the choice to take him for the full price or to leave him. Someone sold a slave saying he is a bread-maker or scribe, then he found him contrary to that, so the buyer has the option: if he wants, he may take him by paying the full price, and if he wants, he may return him. Because his desire decreased due to the missing quality and the seller broke his promise. If the buyer wants to take him, he must pay the agreed price; there is no reduction for the missing quality. However, if the seller agrees to a reduction, it is permissible as a separate transaction. Proof from hadith: 'When you make a sale, say: No deception.' (Bukhari no. 2117, Tirmidhi)
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling on khiyar al-wasf (option due to missing described quality). If a seller describes a slave with a specific craft (like baking or writing) and the slave lacks that quality, the buyer has an option (khiyar) to either accept the slave at the full agreed price or return him. The commentary explains that the buyer cannot demand a price reduction because the missing quality does not have a separate market value; the option is either to take or to leave. This is based on the hadith 'La khilabah' (no deception), which encourages honesty. The author notes that if the seller voluntarily offers a reduction, it is a separate agreement. The ruling applies to any sale where a specific quality is explicitly stated and found wanting. The option is absolute: the buyer cannot claim a proportional price reduction.

Key Terms
لا خلابة (la khilabah): A declaration meaning 'no deception' or 'no cheating,' recommended for the seller to ensure transparency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a slave is sold as a baker but is not, what are the buyer's options according to this passage?
A) Pay a reduced price or return
B) Accept at full price or return the slave
C) Only return the slave
D) Sue the seller for damages

Key Takeaway
If a sold item lacks an expressly described quality, the buyer may only accept it at full price or return it; no price reduction is allowed.

Khiyar al-Shart Does Not Transfer to Heirs Upon Death
Ruling on khiyar al-shart transfer with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the transfer of khiyar al-shart upon death and explain the difference with the Shafi'i position, citing the textual evidence.

Core Idea
Death voids the option of stipulation; it does not pass to heirs.

In Hanafi sales law, when a party dies during the option period, the fate of their contractual right depends on the type of option. This passage from the chapter on sales (Kitab al-Buyu') addresses the specific case of khiyar al-shart (option of stipulation). It rules that death voids the option entirely, contrary to the Shafi'i view that heirs inherit it. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly determining the binding status of a sale after a party's death.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what happens to khiyar al-shart when the holder dies: the option becomes void and does not transfer to heirs. The sale becomes binding immediately.
The passage explicitly states: 'If the one who has the option dies, his option becomes void and does not transfer to his heirs.'
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees: he holds that khiyar al-shart transfers to heirs, similar to other options like khiyar al-‘ayb and khiyar al-ta‘yin.
The text records: 'Imam Shafi'i says: Just as the option of defect and the option of designation transfer to the heirs, similarly the option of stipulation also transfers to the heirs.'
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i analogy: khiyar al-shart is like other options in that it involves a right that can be exercised by heirs. Therefore, it should transfer.
The Shafi'i proof is qiyas (analogy) on options that do transfer.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal: (1) A hadith restricts the option to the two contracting parties only. (2) Khiyar al-shart is based on personal will (irada), which is intangible and cannot be inherited. In contrast, khiyar al-‘ayb and khiyar al-ta‘yin are based on objective circumstances that heirs can evaluate.
The hadith from Ibn Umar (ra) says: 'The two parties of a sale each have the option...' The Hanafi argument distinguishes personal stipulation from defects/choices.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: In the Hanafi school, if the party dies during the option period, the contract becomes binding immediately. In the Shafi'i school, the heir has the right to cancel or confirm the sale for the remainder of the period.
This difference matters in estate and contract law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاذا مات من له الخيار بطل خياره ولم ينتقل الى ورثته [۸۵۸ (۱۱) ومن کرنے کی اطلاع دیدی جائے۔ ۱۸۵۷ (۱۰) پس اگرجس کو خیار تھاوہ مرگیا تواس کا نتیار باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اور یہ اس کے ورثہ کی طرف منتقل نہیں ہوگا۔ بائع یا مشتری جس نے خیار شرط لیا تھا وہ مر گیا تو اب یہ اختیار اس کے ورثہ کی طرف منتقل نہیں ہو گا۔ اور وارث کو اس بیچ کا خیار شرط نہیں ہوگا ۔ بلکہ چونکہ پہلے ایجاب اور قبول ہو چکے ہیں اس لئے بیچ لازم ہو جائے گی۔ یہ اختیار، ارادے اور چاہت کا نام ہے کہ بیع جائز قرار دیں یا نہ دیں۔ ورنہ ایجاب اور قبول پہلے ہو چکے ہیں۔ اور ارادے معنوی شی ہیں وہ منتقل نہیں ہوتے اس لئے اختیار ورثہ کی طرف منتقل نہیں ہو گا (۲) حدیث میں اشارہ ہے عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رسول الله الله قال المتبايعان كل واحد منهما بالخيار على صاحبه مالم يتفرقا الا بيع الخيار (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب البیعان بالخیار مالم يتفرقا ص ۲۸۳ نمبر ۱۲۱۱۱) اس حدیث میں صرف المتبايعان یعنی بائع اور مشتری کو اختیار دیا گیا ہے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ کسی اور کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہوگا۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جسطرح خیار عیب اور خیار تعین ورثہ کی طرف منتقل ہوتا ہے اسی طرح خیار شرط بھی ورثہ کی طرف منتقل ہوگا۔ اور اس کو بھی بیع توڑنے اور جائز قرار دینے کا حق ہوگا۔
If the one who has the option dies, his option becomes void and does not transfer to his heirs. (857 (10)) So if the one who had the option dies, his option becomes void. And it does not transfer to his heirs. The seller or buyer who had stipulated the option dies, now this option does not transfer to his heirs. And the heir will not have the option of stipulation in this sale. Rather, since the offer and acceptance have already occurred, the sale becomes binding. This option is the name of will and desire, to make the sale valid or not. Otherwise, offer and acceptance have already occurred. And wills are intangible things; they do not transfer, therefore the option does not transfer to the heirs. (2) There is indication in the hadith: From Abdullah ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The two parties of a sale each have the option against the other as long as they have not separated, except the sale of option.' (Bukhari, Book of Sale, Chapter: The Two Parties Have Option as Long as They Have Not Separated, p. 283 no. 12111) In this hadith, only the two parties, i.e., the seller and the buyer, are given the option. This means that no one else has this option. Imam Shafi'i says: Just as the option of defect and the option of designation transfer to the heirs, similarly the option of stipulation also transfers to the heirs. And he too will have the right to cancel or validate the sale.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the chapter on sales (Kitab al-Buyu') concerning the option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart). The ruling states that if the party who holds this option dies, the option becomes void and does not transfer to his heirs. The commentator explains the reasoning: the option is based on personal will and intention (irada wa chahat), which are intangible (ma'nawi) and therefore cannot be inherited. Since the offer and acceptance have already taken place, the sale becomes binding upon death. The proof is a hadith from Ibn Umar (ra) in which the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) restricts the option to the two contracting parties, implying that no one else—including heirs—inherits it. The passage then records a disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i, who analogizes khiyar al-shart to khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect) and khiyar al-ta'yin (option of specification), both of which transfer to heirs. The Hanafi response, implied by the text, is that those options are based on objective conditions (like defects or choices) that heirs can act upon, whereas khiyar al-shart is a personal stipulation. The Hanafi position is that the option is voided by death and the contract becomes binding.

Key Terms
خیار شرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated by one or both parties to a sale to cancel or confirm the contract within a specified period.
خیار عیب (khiyar al-‘ayb): The buyer's option to return a purchased item if a pre-existing defect is discovered.
خیار تعین (khiyar al-ta‘yin): The buyer's right to choose one item among several purchased in a single contract, usually with a time limit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a buyer who has stipulated an option (khiyar al-shart) dies before the option period expires, what happens to the option?
A) It transfers to his heirs.
B) It becomes void.
C) It continues until the period ends and then passes to heirs.
D) It is up to the seller to decide.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, khiyar al-shart is a personal right that expires with the holder's death, making the contract binding immediately.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Khiyar al-Sifah: Option for Missing Described Attribute
Ruling that buyer has option to take or leave when described attribute is absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the buyer's options when a described attribute is missing and apply the Hanafi ruling that the buyer cannot demand a price reduction.

Core Idea
A missing described attribute gives the buyer only the option to take at full price or cancel — no price reduction.

This lesson examines khiyar al-sifah, the option based on description. When a seller describes an attribute (e.g., being a baker) and it is absent, the buyer may either accept the item at the agreed price or void the sale. The key Hanafi principle is that attributes have no independent price, so the buyer cannot claim a reduction. We'll explore the ruling, its evidence from hadith, and the underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the buyer's options
Read the passage: a slave is sold with a described attribute (baker/scribe) but the attribute is missing. The buyer has two options: take at full price or cancel.
Note that the buyer cannot demand a partial refund.
2
Understand why no price reduction is allowed
The passage explains that an attribute does not have an independent price (sifat ke muqable mein mustaqil qeemat nahi hoti). Therefore, the buyer cannot claim a reduction for the missing attribute.
This is a fundamental Hanafi principle in khiyar al-sifah.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The proof is from the hadith in which the Prophet ﷺ said 'la khilaba' (no deception) to a man who was deceived in sales. This implies that deception gives the buyer a right to cancel.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Tirmidhi, and its chain is considered zanni al-thubut.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) allow a price reduction (arsh) for missing attributes, but the Hanafi school restricts the remedy to acceptance or cancellation.
This is a thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in the buyer's remedy.
5
Apply the ruling to a contemporary case
Consider buying a car advertised with a sunroof but delivered without it. The buyer may return the car or keep it at the full price—not demand a discount. If the seller agrees to reduce, it is a new transaction.
The same principle applies to any described attribute in a sale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کسی نے غلام بیچا یہ کہ کر کہ یہ روٹی پکانے والا یا کا تب ہے پس اس کو اس کے خلاف پایا تو مشتری کو اس کا اختیار ہے کہ اگر چا ہے تو پوراشن دے کر لے اور اگر چاہے تو اس کو چھوڑ دے۔ غلام بیچا یہ کہہ کر کہ یہ روٹی پکانے والا ہے لیکن بعد میں پتہ چلا کہ وہ صفت اس غلام میں نہیں ہے تو اس صفت کے نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے مشتری کو بیع جائز قرار دینے اور بیچ کے توڑنے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ صفت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کی رغبت کم ہوگئی اور بائع نے خلاف وعدہ کیا اس لئے اس کو توڑنے کا حق ہو گا۔ اور اگر غلام لینا چاہے تو جو قیمت آپس میں طے ہوئی تھی وہی قیمت دے کر لینا ہوگا۔ روٹی پکانا کاتب ہونا یہ صفت ہے اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ صفت کے مقابلے میں مستقل قیمت نہیں ہوتی اس لئے اس صفت کی کمی کی وجہ سے قیمت میں کمی نہیں ہوگی۔ وت ہاں ! بائع قیمت کم کرنے پر راضی ہو جائے تو گویا کہ الگ صفقہ کے ماتحت کم ہوئی جس کی گنجائش ہے۔ البتہ قانونی طور پر پہلی ہی قیمت میں لینا ہوگا۔ اس کا ثبوت حدیث سے ملتا ہے عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رجلا ذكر للنبى الله انه يخدع في البيوع فقال اذا بايعت فقل لا خلابة (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب ما يكره من الخداع في البيع ص ۲۸۴ نمبر ۲۱۱۷ / ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فیمن سخدع فی حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا بائع اور مشترکی دونوں کو اپنے صاحب پر اختیار ہے جب تک کہ جدا نہ ہو جائے مگر خیار شرط کے بیع میں (ب) آپ کے سامنے تذکرہ آیا کہ ایک آدمی بیچ میں دھو کہ کھا جاتا ہے تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ جب آپ بیچ کریں تو کہہ دیا کریں کہ دھوکہ نہیں (نوٹ) دوسری حدیث میں آپ کو تین دن کا اختیار لینے کو فرمایا تھا ) باع عبدا على انه خباز او كاتب فوجده بخلاف ذلک فالمشترى بالخيار ان شاء اخذه بجميع الثمن وان شاء تركه. البیع ص ۲۳۶ نمبر ۱۲۵۰) اس حدیث میں صحابی بیچ میں دھو کہ کھاتے تھے تو اس کو اختیار لینے کے لئے کہا گیا ہے۔ اس لئے جو لوگ صفت میں دھو کہ کھا جائے اس کو بیع توڑنے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ صفت مرغوب فیہ کے فوت ہونے سے مشتری کو بیع توڑنے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ خباز : روٹی پکانے والا حیز کا اسم فاعل ہے۔
Someone sold a slave saying that he is a baker or a scribe, then found him contrary to that, so the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he may take him with the full price, and if he wishes, he may leave him. The slave was sold saying that he is a baker, but later it was discovered that the attribute is not in this slave, so due to the absence of that attribute, the buyer has the option to validate the sale or cancel it. Because the absence of that attribute reduced his desire, and the seller broke his promise, so he has the right to cancel. And if he wants to take the slave, he must take him with the price that was agreed upon. Baking or being a scribe is an attribute, and it has already passed that an attribute does not have an independent price, so due to the lack of this attribute, the price does not decrease. But if the seller agrees to reduce the price, then it is as if it decreased under a separate transaction, which is permissible. However, legally, he must take it at the first price. Its proof comes from the hadith: From Abdullah ibn Umar that a man mentioned to the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he was deceived in sales, so he said: 'When you buy, say: "No deception."' (Bukhari, Book of Sale, Chapter: What is Disliked of Deception in Sale, p. 284 no. 2117 / Tirmidhi, Book of Sale, Chapter: What Came About the One Who is Deceived in Sale, footnote: (a) He said: The buyer and seller both have option against each other as long as they have not separated except in the sale of option. (b) It was mentioned to him that a man is deceived in sales, so he said: When you buy, say: 'No deception.' Note: In another hadith, he was given the option of three days.) He sold a slave on the condition that he is a baker or scribe, but he found him contrary to that, so the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he takes him with all the price, and if he wishes, he leaves him. (Sale, p. 236 no. 1250) In this hadith, the companion was being deceived in sales, so he was told to take the option. Therefore, those who are deceived in an attribute have the option to cancel the sale. Due to the loss of a desirable attribute, the buyer has the option to cancel. 'Khabbaz' means baker; it is the active participle of the verb 'to bake'.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the option of description (khiyar al-sifah). The scenario: a person sells a slave describing him as a baker (khabbaz) or scribe (katib), but the slave is found not to possess that attribute. The buyer has the option: either accept the slave at the full agreed price, or cancel the sale. The commentator explains that the absence of a desirable attribute reduces the buyer's inclination (raghbat) and the seller broke his promise, so cancellation is justified. However, the buyer cannot demand a price reduction because an attribute does not have an independent price (sifat ke muqable mein mustaqil qeemat nahi hoti). The only remedies are acceptance at full price or cancellation. If the seller voluntarily agrees to reduce the price, it is a new separate transaction. The proof comes from the hadith in which the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) instructed a man who was deceived in sales to say 'la khilaba' (no deception), indicating that deception gives the buyer a right to cancel. Additionally, the hadith of Ibn Umar about the two parties having option is referenced. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi principle that options based on description give the buyer the right to rescind but not to reduce the price.

Key Terms
اختیار (ikhtiyar): Option or choice; used here to refer to the buyer's right to take or cancel the sale.
خباز (khabbaz): Baker; a person whose profession is baking bread.
کاتب (katib): Scribe or writer; a person who can write, considered a desirable skill.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He can demand a partial refund.
B) He can take the slave at full price or cancel the sale.
C) He must accept the slave at a reduced price.
D) He has no remedy because the sale was unconditional.

Key Takeaway
When a described attribute is missing, the buyer’s remedy is limited to accepting at full price or cancelling the sale; no price reduction is allowed.

Option of Description (Khiyar al-Wasf) in Slave Sale
Ruling when purchased slave lacks specified skill

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a purchased slave lacks a stipulated skill and apply the option of description (khiyar al-wasf).

Core Idea
Missing a described attribute gives the buyer the option to return the slave – not a void sale, but a choice.

This lesson covers a standard Hanafi ruling when a seller describes a slave as having a specific skill, like being a baker or scribe, but the buyer finds otherwise. The passage from al-Sharh al-Thamiri explains that the sale remains valid, but the buyer gains the right to either keep the slave at the full price or return him. This is based on a hadith granting an option to a companion who was deceived in a sale. Understanding this ruling clarifies the Hanafi concept of khiyar al-wasf (option of description).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is selling a slave described as a baker or scribe, but the skill is absent. The ruling: the sale is valid but the buyer has a khiyar (option) to keep or return.
The ruling is not invalidation but a choice.
2
Locate the Dalil
The author cites a hadith from al-Bay' where a companion was given an option when deceived in a sale.
The hadith serves as the proof for the option.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The hadith indicates that deception (or missing attribute) in a sale gives the buyer the right to cancel. The missing description is treated as a form of deception triggering khiyar.
The Hanafi school extends this to any missing desired attribute.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Other schools may not grant an option for missing description unless it was explicitly stipulated as a condition. The Hanafi school grants it even if implied as a description.
The practical difference is that the Hanafi option is broader.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The Hanafi position as per Zahir al-Riwayah is mufta bihi: the buyer has the option. No intra-Hanafi disagreement is recorded here.
This ruling is relied upon in fatwa.

كتاب البيوع
باع عبدا على انه خباز او كاتب فوجده بخلاف ذلك فالمشترى بالخيار ان شاء اخذه بجميع الثمن وان شاء تركه.
البیع ص ۲۳۶ نمبر ۱۲۵۰) اس حديث ميں صحابی بيچ ميں دھو کہ[؟] کھاتے تھے تو اس کو اختیار لينے کے ليے کہا گيا ہے۔ اس ليے جو لوگ صفت ميں دھو کہ[؟] کھا جائے اس کو بيع توڑنے کا اختیار ہوگا۔

Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part Two, Book of Sales. He sold a slave on the condition that he is a baker or a scribe, and he found him contrary to that, so the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he takes him with the full price, and if he wishes, he leaves him. (Al-Bay' p. 236 no. 1250) In this hadith, the companion used to cheat in selling, so he was told to have the option. Therefore, whoever is cheated in a description, he will have the option to cancel the sale. Due to the loss of the desired attribute, the buyer has the option to cancel the sale. Khabbaz: the active participle for bread-baker.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-wasf (option of description). The ruling states that if a slave is sold with the condition that he is a baker or scribe, and the buyer finds him lacking that skill, the buyer has the option to either keep the slave at the full price or return him. The Urdu commentary explains that the basis is a hadith in which a companion was given the option when he was deceived in a sale. The lesson is that when a desired attribute is absent, the buyer may cancel the sale. The term 'خباز' is the active participle for baker.

Key Terms
خباز (khabbaz): Baker; the active participle from خبز (khabz).
كاتب (katib): Scribe; one who writes.
خيار (khiyar): Option; the right to affirm or rescind a sale.
صفت (sifat): Attribute; the quality stipulated in the sale.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sale, if a stipulated attribute is missing, the buyer has the option to keep the item at full price or return it.

Khiyar al-Ru'yah: The Option of Inspection
Defining khiyar al-ru'yah and its three rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three rulings of khiyar al-ru'yah and explain why only the buyer has the option to rescind upon seeing an unseen item.

Core Idea
A sale of an unseen item is valid, but only the buyer may rescind upon inspection.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri introduces khiyar al-ru'yah, a key concept in Hanafi sales law. It lays out three clear rulings, grounded in a hadith, and explains the reasoning behind each. Understanding this option will help you navigate transactions where goods are purchased without prior inspection, a common scenario in modern commerce.

Guided Path
1
State the three rulings
Read the three numbered sentences in the passage. Identify each as a distinct rule: (1) validity, (2) buyer's option, (3) seller's no option.
2
Identify the hadith proof
Locate the hadith of Abu Hurairah cited in the text. Note the exact wording: 'من اشترى شيئا لم يره فهو بالخيار إذا راه'.
This is the primary dalil for the buyer's option.
3
Analyze the reasoning for the seller's exclusion
Read the commentary explaining why the seller has no option. The hadith says 'من اشترى' not 'من باع'. Also, the seller had access to the item.
This is based on both textual and rational reasoning.
4
Consider the cross-madhhab dispute
Note that Imam Shafi'i does not give the option if the item was described. Understand the Hanafi response that seeing is essential for full consent.
This is an example of legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرح الثميرى الجزء الثانى
كتاب البيوع
باب خيار الرؤية
[۸۵۹] (۱) ومن اشترى مالم يره فالبيع جائز [۸۶۰] (۲) وله الخيار اذا رأه ان شاء اخذه وان شاء رده [۸۶۱](۳) ومن باع مالم يره فلا خيار له.
باب خيار الرؤية
ضروری نوٹ کسی چیز کو دیکھے بغیر خرید لے تو اس وقت دیکھنے کے بعد چاہے تو خریدے اور چاہے تو نہ خریدے ایسے اختیار کو خیار رویت کہتے ہیں۔ خیار رویت جائز ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابی هريرة قال قال رسول الله من اشترى شيئا لم يره فهو بالخيار اذا راه (الف) ( دار قطنی ، کتاب البیوع ج ثالث ص ۵ نمبر ۲۷۷۹ سفن للبیھقی[؟] ، باب من قال مجوز بیج العین العالمية[؟] ج خامس ص ۴۴۰ نمبر ۱۰۴۲۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مبیع کو نہ دیکھا ہو تو دیکھنے کے بعد اس کو لینے اور نہ لینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔
[۸۵۹] (۱) کسی نے خریدا ایسی چیز کو جس کو دیکھا نہیں تو بیع جائز ہے۔ بغیر دیکھے بھی کسی چیز کو بیچنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ مال ہے اور جھگڑا بھی نہیں ہوگا، کیونکہ دیکھ لینے کے بعد پسند نہ آئے تو بیع توڑ دے گا (۲) اوپر کی حدیث سے بھی پتہ چلا کہ بغیر ديكھے چیز خرید سکتا ہے۔
[۸۶۰] (۲) اور مشتری کو اختیار ہوگا جب بیع کو دیکھے چاہے تو اس کو لے لے اور چاہے تو اس کو واپس کر دے۔ دیکھنے کے بعد مشتری کو لینے اور نہ لینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔ کیونکہ دیکھنے سے پہلے اس کی رغبت کا علم نہیں ہے اور نہ وہ اس پر راضی ہے۔ اور پہلے گزر گیا کہ رضامندی کے بغیر بیع نہیں ہوگی (۲) اوپر حدیث گزری عن ابی هريرة قال قال رسول الله الا الله[؟] من اشترى شيئا لم يره فهو بالخيار اذا راه (ب) دارقطنی، کتاب البیوع ج ثالث ص ۵ نمبر ۲۷۷۹ / مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۲ فی الرجل اشتری ولا ینظر الیہ من قال هو بالخيار اذا راه ان شاء اخذ وان شاء ترک، ج رابع ، ص ۲۷۳، نمبر ۱۹۹۶۷ ) اس حدیث سے پتہ چلا کہ دیکھنے کے بعد مشتری کو لینے اور نہ لینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔
[۸۶۱] (۳) کسی نے بیچا ایسی چیز کو جس کو دیکھا نہیں تو اس کو اختیار نہیں ہوگا۔ بائع نے بغیر دیکھے بیع بیچ دی اور بعد میں خیار رویت لینا چاہتا ہے۔ اور دیکھنے کے بعد خیار رویت کے ماتحت بیع توڑنا چاہتا ہے تو اس کو خیار رویت کے ماتحت بیع توڑنے کا اختیار نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ (۱) کیونکہ وہ چیز اس کے پاس تھی۔ اس نے بیچنے سے پہلے کیوں نہیں دیکھی؟ نہ دیکھنا یہ اس کی غلطی تھی اس لئے اس کو خیار رویت نہیں دیا جائے گا (۲) اوپر کی حدیث میں من اشتری شیئا فرمایا ہے کہ جس نے خریدا، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ خریدنے والے کو اختیار ہوگا۔ من باع نہیں فرمایا
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا جس نے کسی ایسی چیز کو خریدا جس کو دیکھا نہیں ہے تو اختیار ہے جب اس کو دیکھ لے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا جس نے کسی ایسی چیز کو خریدا جس کو دیکھا نہیں ہے تو اختیار ہے جب اس کو دیکھ لے۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part Two, Book of Sales. Chapter on Option of Inspection. [859] (1) Whoever buys what he has not seen, the sale is valid. [860] (2) And he has the option when he sees it: if he wishes, he takes it; if he wishes, he returns it. [861] (3) And whoever sells what he has not seen, he has no option. Chapter on Option of Inspection. Essential note: If someone takes an item without seeing it, then after seeing it, he may either buy it or not buy it – such an option is called khiyar al-ru'yah. Khiyar al-ru'yah is valid; its proof is the hadith from Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever buys something he has not seen, he has the option when he sees it.' (A) (Daraqutni, Kitab al-Buyu', vol. 3, p. 5, no. 2779; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, ...) From this hadith it is understood that if the sold item has not been seen, then after seeing, he has the option to take or not. [859] (1) Someone bought an item that he had not seen – the sale is valid. It is also valid to sell an item without seeing, because it is property and there will be no dispute, since if after seeing he does not like it, he can cancel the sale. (2) From the above hadith it is also learned that one may buy a thing without seeing. [860] (2) And the buyer will have the option when he sees the sold item: he may take it or return it. After seeing, the buyer has the option to take or not, because before seeing his inclination is not known and he is not satisfied with it, and it has passed that a sale without consent is not valid. (2) The above hadith passed: from Abu Hurairah, the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever buys something he has not seen, he has the option when he sees it.' (B) (Daraqutni, Kitab al-Buyu', vol. 3, p. 5, no. 2779; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, ...) From this hadith it is learned that after seeing, the buyer has the option to take or not. [861] (3) Someone sold an item that he had not seen – he will have no option. The seller sold without seeing and later wants to claim khiyar al-ru'yah, and after seeing wants to cancel the sale under khiyar al-ru'yah – he will not be given the option to cancel under khiyar al-ru'yah. (1) Because the item was in his possession; why did he not see it before selling? Not seeing was his fault, so he will not be given khiyar al-ru'yah. (2) In the above hadith it is said 'whoever buys', meaning the one who buys gets the option; it did not say 'whoever sells'. Footnote: (A) He said: Whoever buys something he has not seen, he has the option when he sees it. (B) He said: Whoever buys something he has not seen, he has the option when he sees it.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on khiyar al-ru'yah (option of inspection), which is a specific branch of option in Hanafi sales law. The text first gives three numbered rulings: (1) buying an unseen object is valid, (2) the buyer has the option upon seeing to either keep or return it, and (3) the seller has no such option. The Urdu commentary explains the definition, proof from a hadith of Abu Hurairah, and the reasoning: before seeing, the buyer cannot be sure of his desire; consent is essential for a sale. The third ruling is justified by the explicit wording of the hadith (buyer only) and by logic: the seller had access to the item and should have inspected it before selling. The footnote repeats the hadith twice.

Key Terms
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): Option of inspection; the buyer's right to annul the sale after seeing an unseen item.
مشتری (mushtari): Buyer; the party who purchases.
بائع (ba'i'): Seller; the party who sells.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone sells an item he has never seen, does he have the option to cancel the sale upon seeing it?
A) Yes, because he did not see it.
B) No, because the hadith grants the option only to the buyer.
C) Yes, but only if the buyer agrees.
D) No, because seeing is not required.

Key Takeaway
The sale of an unseen item is valid, but only the buyer has the option to rescind upon inspection; the seller does not.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
6 min
Rulings of Khiyar al-Ru'yah: The Option of Inspection
Complete page covering khiyar al-ru'yah for buyer and seller with hadith and athar proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three rulings on khiyar al-ru'yah for buyer and seller, and explain the hadith proof that limits the option to the buyer.

Core Idea
The buyer of an unseen item has the option to confirm or cancel upon seeing; the seller has no such option.

When you buy something without seeing it first, are you stuck with the purchase? Islamic law provides a protection called khiyar al-ru'yah (option of inspection). This lesson examines the core rulings from the Hanafi madhhab: that the sale is valid, the buyer has the right to cancel upon seeing, and the seller has no such right. We will explore the hadith evidence that establishes this option exclusively for the buyer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states three rulings: (1) sale of an unseen item is valid, (2) the buyer has an option upon seeing, (3) the seller has no option. Note that the sale is not suspended or void; it is immediately valid but revocable by the buyer.
This is the foundation: the sale is jā'iz (valid) but not binding until the buyer inspects.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Abu Huraira: 'Whoever buys something he has not seen, he has the option when he sees it.' The source also cites the practice of the Companions (e.g., the case of Uthman and Talha) to reinforce the buyer-only rule.
The hadith is recorded by al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi, and is considered ahad (single-narrator) but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly says 'man ishtara' (whoever buys) – this specifies the buyer. The phrase 'فهو بالخيار' (he has the option) grants a legal right. The wording does not extend to the seller. Also, the seller owned the item and should have inspected it before selling; his failure is his own negligence.
Thus the proof is direct and unambiguous, giving a qat'i (definitive) indication even though the transmission is zanni.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some non‑Hanafi schools grant the seller khiyar al‑ru'yah if he also had not seen the item. The Hanafi position rejects this based on the explicit hadith wording and the principle that the seller's negligence negates his claim.
The ikhtilaf is practical: if the item appreciates, the seller might want to cancel, but Hanafi law prevents that.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the explicit text and the Companion practice (arbiter Jubayr ibn Mut'im's verdict). Therefore the mufta bihi (operative position) is that only the buyer has khiyar al‑ru'yah.
This tarjih is based on strength of textual evidence, not mere juristic preference.

Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part Two, 28, Book of Sales, Chapter of Khiyar al-Ru'yah. [859] (1) Whoever buys something he has not seen, the sale is valid. [860] (2) He has the option when he sees it: if he wishes he takes it, and if he wishes he returns it. [861] (3) Whoever sells something he has not seen, there is no option for him. Chapter of Khiyar al-Ru'yah. Essential note: If someone buys an item without seeing it, then upon seeing he may buy or not; such an option is called khiyar al-ru'yah. Khiyar al-ru'yah is permissible. Its proof is this hadith: From Abu Huraira: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever buys something he has not seen, he has the option when he sees it.' (a) (al-Daraqutni, Kitab al-Buyu', vol. 3, p. 5, no. 2779; al-Bayhaqi, Bab man ajaza bay' al-'ayn al-gha'ibah, vol. 5, p. 440, no. 10426). From this hadith it is known that if the sold object has not been seen, then after seeing there will be an option to take or not. [859] (1) Someone bought an item which he had not seen, the sale is valid. Selling an item without seeing it is also valid, because it is property and there will be no dispute, because after seeing if he does not like it, he will break the sale. (2) Also from the above hadith it is known that one can buy an item without seeing. [860] (2) And the buyer will have the option when he sees the sale item: if he wishes he takes it, and if he wishes he returns it. After seeing, the buyer will have the option to take or not. Because before seeing his inclination is not present and he is not satisfied. And it has passed that a sale without satisfaction is not valid. (2) The above hadith passed: 'Whoever buys something he has not seen, he has the option when he sees it.' (b) (al-Daraqutni, Kitab al-Buyu', vol. 3, p. 5, no. 2779; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah: 'Concerning a man who buys without looking at it; he who said he has the option when he sees it: if he wishes he takes, if he wishes he leaves', vol. 4, p. 273, no. 19967). From this hadith it is known that after seeing the buyer will have the option to take or not. [861] (3) Someone sold an item which he had not seen, then he will have no option. The seller sold without seeing, and later wants to claim khiyar al-ru'yah, and after seeing wants to break the sale under khiyar al-ru'yah, then he will not be given the option to break the sale. (1) The item was with him. Why did he not see it before selling? Not seeing it was his mistake, therefore he will not be given khiyar al-ru'yah. (2) In the above hadith it is said 'whoever buys', implying that the buyer has the option. It did not say 'whoever sells'. Footnote: (a) He said: 'Whoever buys something he has not seen, he has the option when he sees it.' (b) He said: 'Whoever buys something he has not seen, he has the option when he sees it.'
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This is a passage from al-Sharh al-Thamiri on the chapter of khiyar al-ru'yah (option of inspection). It presents three matn statements (from the base text) followed by Urdu commentary that explains each ruling and provides proofs. The first ruling (matn 1) states that a sale of an unseen item is valid—it is not void or suspended. The commentary adds that selling unseen is also valid and that the buyer's option prevents disputes. The second ruling (matn 2) establishes the buyer's khiyar: upon seeing the item, he may either accept or reject. The commentary clarifies that this option exists because true consent (rida) is only possible after seeing, and consent is essential for a binding sale. The primary proof is the hadith of Abu Huraira, quoted twice with chains, which explicitly grants the buyer an option. The third ruling (matn 3) states that the seller does not have khiyar al-ru'yah. The commentary argues that since the seller owned the item and could have seen it before selling, his failure to do so is his own fault. Moreover, the hadith wording specifies 'whoever buys', not 'whoever sells'. A supporting athar from Ibn Abi Mulayka recounts that when Uthman sold unseen land to Talha, the arbiter Jubayr ibn Mut'im granted khiyar only to the buyer (Talha), not the seller (Uthman). This establishes the Hanafi position that khiyar al-ru'yah is exclusive to the buyer.

Key Terms
خيار الرؤية (khiyār al-ruʾyah): The option of inspection: the right of the buyer to annul or confirm a sale after seeing the purchased item if it was bought unseen.
مبيع (mabīʿ): The sold item or object of sale.
بائع (bāʾiʿ): The seller.
مشترى (mushtarī): The buyer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, who has khiyar al-ru'yah?
A) Both buyer and seller
B) Only the buyer
C) Only the seller
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, khiyar al-ru'yah is a right exclusively for the buyer, based on the explicit wording of the hadith and the practice of the Companions.

Sufficiency of Representative Seeing in Khiyar al-Ru'yah
Rulings on when partial seeing eliminates the buyer's option.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that khiyar al-ru'yah is eliminated when the buyer sees the representative part of an item as determined by custom ('urf).

Core Idea
Custom defines what is enough seeing to waive khiyar – not every detail must be inspected.

This lesson examines the specific details of khiyar al-ru'yah – the buyer's right to cancel a sale after viewing an unseen item. The Hanafi school clarifies that the buyer need not inspect every part of the item; rather, seeing the portion that customarily reveals the item's condition is sufficient. The matn rulings and their commentary in al-Sharh al-Thamiri provide clear examples and also highlight the dependence on local custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The main ruling: the buyer loses khiyar al-ru'yah (it falls, saqit) when he sees a representative part of the sold item. This is not a universal rule but tied to what is considered sufficient by custom.
The ruling applies to all categories of goods: heaps, garments, slaves, animals, houses.
2
Apply the principle to specific items
For a heap of grain, seeing the top part suffices; for a folded garment, the outer visible part; for a slave-girl, her face; for an animal, its face and hindquarters; for a house, its courtyard (if rooms are uniform). In each case, the seen part reveals the overall quality.
The commentary explains why: e.g., the top of a heap indicates the whole, a face reveals beauty and health, etc.
3
Recognize the role of custom ('urf)
The rule is not fixed but depends on what people customarily consider sufficient. The commentary on the house example adds that where rooms vary, seeing the courtyard alone is not enough; one must see inside the rooms.
This shows that the Hanafi school uses 'urf to determine the threshold of sufficient viewing.
4
Consider the evidence from the footnote
The footnote recounts the story of Caliph Uthman and Talha, where Jubayr ibn Mut'im ruled that the buyer (Talha) retains khiyar because he bought an unseen item, while the seller (Uthman) had seen his item and therefore had no khiyar. This reinforces the principle that khiyar is for the party who has not seen the item.
This story is a practical illustration of khiyar al-ru'yah in early Islamic jurisprudence.

[۸۶۲] (۴) اگر ڈھیر کے اوپر کا حصہ دیکھایا لیٹے کپڑے کے ظاہری حصے کو دیکھایا باندی کا چہرہ دیکھایا جانور کا چہرہ دیکھا اور اس کا پچھلا حصہ دیکھا تو اس کے لئے خیار رویت نہیں ہے۔
اشر مبیع کے ہر ہر عضو کو دیکھنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ عرف میں جس عضو یا جس حصے کو دیکھنا شمار کیا جاتا ہے اس حصے کو دیکھنا کافی سمجھا جائے گا۔ اور اسی کو دیکھنے سے خیار رویت ختم ہو جائے گا۔ مثلا ڈھیر کے اوپر کے حصے کو دیکھنے سے پورے ڈھیر کی معلومات ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے اوپر کے حصے کو دیکھنا کافی ہو گا۔ اسی طرح باندی کے چہرے کو دیکھنے سے پوری باندی کا علم ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے چہرہ دیکھنے سے خیار رویت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ جانور کے چہرے اور سرین کو دیکھنے سے پورا علم ہوتا ہے اور اس لئے انہیں کو دیکھنے سے خیار رویت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ انواں جس حصے کے دیکھنے سے پوری طبیع کا علم ہو جائے اس حصے کے دیکھنے سے خیار رویت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ ات مطويا : لپیٹا ہوا۔ کفل : جانور کی سرین۔
[۸۶۳] (۵) اور اگر گھر کے صحن کو دیکھا تو مشتری کو اختیار نہیں ہو گا چاہے اس کے کمروں کو نہ دیکھا ہو۔ ری مصنف کے ملک میں کمرے ایک طرح کے ہوا کرتے تھے اور محن کو دیکھنے سے کمروں کا اندازہ ہو جاتا تھا اس لئے فرمایا کہ محن کے دیکھنے سے خیار رویت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ چاہے کمروں کو نہ دیکھا ہو۔ لیکن جن ملکوں میں کمرے کے اندر کا حصہ الگ الگ انداز کا ہو ان ملکوں میں کمرے کے اندر دیکھنا ہوگا۔ اس کے بغیر خیار رویت ساقط نہیں ہو گا وجہ اور اصول او پر گزر گئے۔
حاشیہ : (ب) ابن ابی ملیکہ سے روایت ہے کہ حضرت عثمان نے طلحہ بن عبید اللہ سے مدینہ میں زمین خریدی کوفہ میں زمین کی بدلے میں مال غنیمت میں ملی تھی۔ پس جب دونوں جدا ہوئے تو حضرت عثمان کو ندامت ہوئی پھر فرمایا میں نے ایسی چیز بیچی جو دیکھی نہیں ہے تو حضرت طلحہ نے فرمایا خیار رویت مجھے ہوگی۔ اس لئے کہ میں نے غائبانہ کی چیز خریدی ہے۔ بہر حال آپ نے دیکھا ہے جس کو چا ہے۔ تو دونوں نے حضرت جبیر بن مطعم کو کم بنایا تو انہوں نے حضرت عثمان کے خلاف فیصلہ فرمایا کہ بیع جائز ہے اور خیار رویت حضرت طلحہ کے لئے ہے۔ اس لئے کہ انہوں نے غیبوبت کی چیز خریدی ہے۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part Two, 29, Book of Sales. [862] (4) And if he looks at the top of a heap, or at the outer part of a folded garment, or at the face of a slave-girl, or at the face of an animal and its hind part, then there is no option for him. [863] (5) And if he sees the courtyard of a house, then there is no option for him, even if he did not see... so there is no option. [862] (4) If he saw the upper part of a heap, or the apparent part of a folded cloth, or the face of a slave-girl, or the face of an animal and its hind part, then he has no khiyar al-ru'yah. Explanation: It is not necessary to see every single part of the sold item. Rather, according to custom, seeing the part that is considered sufficient for identification is enough, and by seeing that, the khiyar al-ru'yah is removed. For example, seeing the upper part of a heap gives knowledge of the whole heap, so seeing the upper part is sufficient. Similarly, seeing the face of a slave-girl gives knowledge of the whole slave-girl, so seeing the face removes the khiyar. Seeing the face and hindquarters of an animal gives full knowledge, so seeing these removes the khiyar. In short, seeing the part that allows full awareness of the item eliminates the khiyar. 'Mutan' means folded; 'kafal' means hindquarters. [863] (5) And if he sees the courtyard of a house, then the buyer has no option, even if he did not see its rooms. In the author's country, rooms were of a uniform type, and seeing the courtyard gave an idea of the rooms, so it was said that seeing the courtyard removes the khiyar, even if the rooms were not seen. But in countries where the interior of rooms are different, then one must see inside the rooms; without that, the khiyar is not removed. The reason and principle have passed earlier. Footnote: (b) Ibn Abi Mulayka narrates that Uthman bought land in Madinah from Talha ibn Ubayd Allah in exchange for land in Kufah that was part of the booty. When they separated, Uthman regretted and said: 'I sold something I had not seen.' Talha said: 'The khiyar is for me, because I bought an unseen item. You, on the other hand, saw what you bought.' So they appointed Jubayr ibn Mut'im as arbiter, and he ruled against Uthman that the sale is valid and khiyar is for Talha, because he bought an unseen item.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage from al-Sharh al-Thamiri continues the chapter on khiyar al-ru'yah by specifying what constitutes sufficient seeing to eliminate the buyer's option. Two matn rulings are presented. The first (matn 4) states that looking at the visible representative part of different types of items removes the khiyar: for a heap, the top; for a folded garment, the outer part; for a slave-girl, her face; for an animal, its face and hindquarters. The commentary explains that the principle is not to see every detail but to see enough according to custom ('urf) to form a reasonable judgment of the item. For example, seeing the top of a heap is enough because it indicates the quality of the whole; seeing the face of a slave-girl is sufficient because it reveals her beauty and health; seeing the face and hindquarters of an animal suffices because those parts indicate its condition. The second matn (matn 5) deals with a house: seeing the courtyard alone suffices if the rooms are of a standard type, as was the custom in the author's region. However, the commentary adds a nuance: in places where rooms differ in design, seeing the courtyard alone is not enough; one must see the interior of the rooms. This shows that the rule is not universal but tied to custom ('urf). The footnote at the bottom repeats the story of Uthman and Talha, reinforcing that the buyer (Talha) had khiyar because he bought unseen, while the seller (Uthman) had no khiyar because he had seen his item before selling.

Key Terms
الصبرة (al-ṣubrah): A heap or pile of grain or similar produce.
مطويا (maṭwiyyan): Folded (used for a garment).
الجارية (al-jāriyah): A slave-girl or female servant.
كفل (kafal): The hindquarters or buttocks of an animal.
صحن الدار (ṣaḥn al-dār): The courtyard or open yard of a house.
عرف (ʿurf): Custom or customary practice used to determine what constitutes sufficient seeing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school, what is the general principle for when khiyar al-ru'yah is eliminated?
A) Only if every single part of the item is inspected.
B) When the buyer sees the representative part of the item as determined by custom.
C) When the buyer sees any random part of the item.
D) The khiyar is never eliminated until the buyer explicitly waives it.

Key Takeaway
Seeing the representative part of a sold item according to custom eliminates the buyer's khiyar al-ru'yah; full inspection is not required.

When Partial Inspection Suffices: The Hanafi Rule for Khiyar al-Ru'yah
Ruling on khiyar al-ru'yah with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when the buyer's option of inspection drops upon seeing only a customary part of the sale object, and explain the proof from the athar of 'Uthman and Talhah.

Core Idea
Seeing the customary representative part of an object drops the option of inspection; full inspection is not required.

The option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah) protects a buyer who purchases an unseen item. But what if the buyer sees only part of the item? The Hanafi school rules that seeing the part which customarily gives knowledge of the whole is sufficient. This lesson examines that ruling and the proof from the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a buyer inspecting a sale object. The ruling: if he sees a customary representative part, the option drops.
2
Locate the dalil
The athar from Ibn Abi Mulaykah about 'Uthman and Talhah, recorded by al-Bayhaqi.
This athar is a marfu' report from a Companion.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Jubayr ibn Mut'am's ruling gives option to Talhah (buyer of unseen) and denies to 'Uthman (seller), establishing that the seller has no option and implicitly that seeing the item removes the buyer's option.
The ruling was by arbitration, not a direct legal text.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may require seeing the entire item; Hanafi relies on custom.
The difference is practical: when does the option expire?
5
Apply to examples
Pile of grain (top suffices), folded cloth (apparent side), slave-girl (face), animal (face and rump).
Custom determines what is representative.
